End of Anglo-French Talks; Three-Nation Conference Expands to Five Nations; Italy and Germany Invited to Participate; New Treaty Negotiated to Replace the Locarno Treaty; Door Opened to Rebuilding European Peace; Conference to Be Held Around the Time of the League of Nations General Assembly in September 54

(London) The talks between Britain, France, and Belgium concluded at 6:15 PM. It was resolved to immediately invite Italy and Germany to participate in a future five-nation conference. This conference is scheduled to be held in Brussels. The date will be decided after receiving replies from the governments of Italy and Germany, probably around the time of the League of Nations General Assembly (which convenes in September). As for the guarantee that Britain previously offered to France and Belgium (i.e., mutual assistance to safeguard the security of the two countries' borders), this guarantee will remain valid as long as a solution to the European situation is not reached. How the five-nation conference will proceed is another matter. It is reported that Britain has accepted this arrangement. The issue of the Free City of Danzig was not mentioned in the three-nation talks. (Havas, 23rd)

Three-Nation Communiqué

(London) After deliberating for twelve hours yesterday, the Locarno Treaty signatory nations—Britain, France, and Belgium—reached a complete agreement late at night. After the meeting, the following communiqué was issued: The representatives of France, Belgium, and Britain, noting the arrangements agreed upon on March 19, the proposals made by the German Chancellor on March 31, and the proposals made by the French government on April 8, have resolved the following articles:

(1) The main goal of European nations must be to consolidate peace through a general resolution.

(2) Such a resolution can only be achieved through the free cooperation of the relevant major powers. Nothing is more detrimental to the hope of such a resolution than if European nations are divided into obvious or actual opposing blocs.

(3) Therefore, the three governments believe that a Locarno five-power conference should be convened as soon as it can be conveniently held. In the three countries' opinion, the primary task of this conference should be to negotiate a new treaty to replace the Locarno Rhineland Pact and, through the cooperation of the relevant parties, to resolve the situation caused by Germany's actions on March 7.

(4) Therefore, the three governments propose to consult with the German and Italian governments in the hope that both countries will agree to participate in the proposed conference.

(5) If the conference can make progress, other matters concerning European peace should naturally be brought up for discussion. Under these circumstances, it is hoped that the scope of the discussion will be expanded to facilitate the resolution of these issues through the cooperation of other relevant major powers. The peace of Europe depends on this resolution.

The full text of the communiqué will be jointly sent by Britain, France, and Belgium to the German and Italian governments, and it is hoped that both countries will accept the invitation to the five-power conference and promptly agree on a date for the meeting. British circles highly praise the spirit of cooperation shown by the French and Belgian cabinet members in accommodating the British cabinet members and sincerely participating in new endeavors in order to achieve a lasting European resolution through the free cooperation of all parties. It is said that yesterday's work was based entirely on unity and sincerity. Many view yesterday's compromise as opening up new opportunities for Europe. French opinions believe that the three countries' agreement places primary importance on collective security, and the so-called Four-Power Pact proposal will definitely not be revived. (Reuters, 24th)

Invitation Issued

(Berlin) After conducting talks yesterday, the representatives of Britain, France, and Belgium immediately agreed to convene a five-nation conference to be joined by Italy and Germany to negotiate a new agreement to replace the Locarno Treaty. British Ambassador Sir Phipps and French Ambassador François-Poncet, together with the Belgian Chargé d'Affaires, delivered an invitation to the German government today, formally inviting them to participate in the five-nation conference. (Havas, 24th)

(Rome) French Ambassador Chambrun, British Ambassador Drummond, and Belgian Ambassador Prince de Ligne formally presented an invitation to Foreign Minister Count Ciano, formally inviting Italy to participate in the five-nation conference. (Havas, 24th)

British Aspirations

(London) The highest British foreign affairs authorities have issued an official statement expressing satisfaction with the results of the three-nation talks, especially with France and Belgium's agreement to conduct negotiations with Italy and Germany. It also stated that if a "New Locarno Treaty" cannot be signed, Britain's previous obligations to assist France and Belgium will remain valid. As for the date of the future five-nation conference, it will most likely be around the time of the League of Nations General Assembly in September. The exact date and conference procedures will be decided through diplomatic channels by the countries involved. Britain deeply hopes that the five-nation conference will not limit its efforts to the Western European issue, but will seek a broader solution that includes general European problems. Finally, it stated that the British, French, and Belgian delegations have not only reached an understanding on the procedures for the five-nation conference, but also agree with each other on the fundamental issues to be discussed. The invitation to Germany and Italy to participate in the five-nation conference was issued this evening. Generally, it is believed that after Germany receives the invitation, given the complete harmony of opinions among Britain, France, and Belgium, there will be no further increase in the number of troops stationed in the Rhineland region. (Havas, 23rd)

Paris Satisfied

(Paris) Newspapers here are expressing satisfaction with the talks conducted by the representatives of Britain, France, and Belgium in London yesterday. Le Journal stated, "All parties are very pleased, and the door to peacebuilding has been opened." Le Matin stated, "Britain, France, and Belgium have renewed their efforts for a peaceful situation. It is hoped that Germany will be willing to shake hands with these countries so that a European peace mechanism can be effectively organized." (Havas, 24th)

Resuming Relations with Czechoslovakia: Germany Proposes Two Conditions; Abrogation of Czech-Soviet Alliance and Joining the Four-Power Bloc; Clearly Unacceptable to Czechoslovakia 55

(Paris) Madame Tabouis, a renowned reporter for L'Œuvre, has commented on the talks conducted by the representatives of Britain, France, and Belgium in London yesterday, stating that German leader Hitler intends to propose conditions to the Czechoslovak government to define bilateral relations. This information comes from reliable sources and is known to the representatives of Britain, France, and Belgium. "It is said that Hitler has proposed two demands: (1) All regions of Czechoslovakia where Germans constitute a majority must be designated as autonomous regions and establish federal relations with other parts of Czechoslovakia. (2) Czechoslovakia and other countries of the Little Entente (i.e., Romania and Yugoslavia) may also join the Four-Power Bloc of Britain, France, Germany, and Italy, but Czechoslovakia must abrogate the alliance treaty between Czechoslovakia and the Soviet Union." Debate on Unemployment Relief Bill: Unprecedented Drama in British Parliament; Labour MPs Accuse Sir John Simon of Lying; Sing "The Red Flag" in Unison; Result: Three MPs Suspended for Five Days 59

(London) Last night, during Home Secretary Sir John Simon's defense of the government's proposed unemployment relief bill in the House of Commons, three Independent Labour Party MPs directly accused Simon of lying. The scene was quite chaotic. As a result, these three MPs were punished with temporary suspension. The incident occurred when Simon was delivering his speech enthusiastically, and the entire chamber erupted. Deputy Speaker Sir Herbert promptly announced a temporary recess. Proceedings resumed after more than eighteen minutes. The parliamentary session lasted a total of thirty-six hours and eighteen minutes. At the end, a new and unusual event occurred. When Conservative MPs moved to adjourn the session, someone suddenly started singing "The Red Flag." Labour MPs in the back rows joined in loudly. The names of the three MPs who were punished with temporary suspension last night are as follows: Mr. Buchanan, MP for Glasgow Gorbals; Mr. Stephen, MP for Glasgow Camlachie; and Mr. McGovern, MP for Glasgow Shettleston. This is the first time in the current parliament that such a suspension has occurred. Because it was the first offense for the three MPs in this parliament, they were only fined a suspension of five days and will still receive their parliamentary salaries. Until their return, Mr. Maxton, MP for Glasgow Bridgeton, will be the sole representative of the Independent Labour Party in the House of Commons. The dispute arose because Mr. Buchanan extended his arm and shouted that Sir John Simon was lying. The Deputy Speaker immediately rose to his feet and addressed Buchanan in a stern voice, asking him not to engage in such behavior that violates the rules of parliament. Buchanan was quite angry and continued to denounce Simon. As the disruption increased, Buchanan persisted and refused to listen to advice. The Deputy Speaker then issued a warning, stating that if he did not comply, it was his duty to impose a punishment. Buchanan became enraged and did not stop his abuse. The Deputy Speaker then announced that he would be punished for non-compliance. Sir John Simon immediately proposed a customary motion to suspend his attendance. There was a great uproar in the chamber. Mr. Stephen protested the suspension of his party colleague and criticized Conservative MPs for abusing their power. As the disorder increased, the Deputy Speaker announced a temporary recess. The proceedings had already lasted more than twenty-seven hours. Subsequently, the motions to suspend Buchanan and Stephen were passed by 248 votes to 53 and 256 votes to 51, respectively. However, even after the two MPs left, the dispute continued. When Sir John Simon rose to continue his speech, there was much jeering from the Labour MPs. At this point, Labour MP Mr. Cocks exclaimed, "We all know that Sir John Simon is a liar!" The chair at the time, Speaker Fitzroy, immediately spoke, saying that it would greatly contribute to the maintenance of parliamentary dignity if Cocks could refrain from making such statements. Unexpectedly, Independent Labour Party MP Mr. McGovern suddenly accused Sir John Simon of being a "despicable liar." Because he refused to heed the warning, Simon then proposed a motion to suspend his attendance. A vote was taken and passed by 262 votes to 11. Most of the Labour Party members holding official positions did not participate in the vote. When the Speaker asked McGovern to leave the chamber, McGovern refused. The Sergeant-at-Arms then responded to the Speaker's request and urged him to leave the chamber. Finally, the leader of his party, Mr. Maxton, gently touched his back, and then the Sergeant-at-Arms escorted him out of the chamber, ending the drama. Compared to previous sessions, it seemed quite tame. The cabinet members in attendance laughed heartily. (Reuters, 24th)

Attempt to Assassinate British King: Accused Re-Examined; Preparation for Public Prosecution Under the Treason Act; Defendant's Letter to Simon Read Aloud in Court 60

(London) George Andrew McMahon, who was arrested on the 16th of this month for attempting to assassinate the British King, reappeared in the dock of the Bow Street Magistrates' Court today to be questioned by Sir Campbell. According to Attorney General Sir Somervell, who is prosecuting the case, in addition to the charges of illegally carrying a handgun and intending to endanger life, the defendant will also be publicly prosecuted under the Treason Act of 1842. Sir Somervell further explained that this new charge refers to the provisions of Section 11 of the Act and is not high treason but other statutory minor offenses. The first offense he committed was carrying a gun near the King and attempting to disrupt public order. The second offense was carrying a handgun with the intent to frighten the King. Sir Somervell continued, stating that the day before the incident, McMahon went to a public restaurant near Buckingham Palace, where he dined daily, and told the waitress that they would probably never see each other again, adding that something unexpected would happen and she could learn all about it in the newspapers. On the day of the incident, while the defendant was standing in the crowd watching the procession, he spoke to a mounted police officer and asked him to remove the hideous horse's head. It was also discovered that the defendant had written a short note, apparently to his wife, containing only one sentence, "Please allow me Ireland." As for the handgun that Special Constable Dyke knocked from the defendant's hand, it was loaded with bullets, with only one chamber empty. A pull of the trigger would fire the bullet. After the defendant was arrested, he initially said at the police station, "What I did was right and just. It would not have been difficult for me to shoot the King, but I missed the opportunity." After being questioned by Sir Rollo last week, he added, "I wanted to shoot myself in front of the King, but I failed to do so." (Special Dispatch, 24th)

(London) The defense lawyer for McMahon, the assailant in the assassination attempt on the British King, Mr. Carlsting, read aloud in court today a letter from the defendant to Home Secretary Sir John Simon, in which he described himself as an innocent victim under "organized persecution by your department" because it prevented him from obtaining employment. The letter also stated that he had previously petitioned the King but had not been granted an audience. Now, he demanded complete satisfaction within fourteen hours, or he would exercise his own privilege to obtain appropriate satisfaction. The letter concluded by saying, "This is not an idle threat. I demand fairness, regardless of the outcome." (Reuters, 24th)

Typhoon Causes Disaster in Nagasaki: Houses Collapsed, Ships Lost; Total Damage Estimated at Two Million Yuan 61

Nagasaki: As of noon on the 24th, nine people have been confirmed dead and four injured in the Nagasaki area, which was hit by a typhoon. A total of 59 steamships, civilian ships, and fishing boats have been destroyed, sunk, or washed away. More than 200 houses have collapsed, and approximately 620 houses have been partially damaged. An estimated 550 houses have been flooded, and many other fields and agricultural products have been washed away. The losses in agriculture and forestry alone amount to 1.07 million yuan, and the total losses are expected to exceed 2 million yuan. (Domei, 24th)

Air Defense Drills Completed in Japan's Three Major Cities: 260,000 Personnel Mobilized; Mock Enemy Aircraft Attacked and Repelled 62

(Tokyo) The final act of the large-scale air defense drill took place on the morning of the 24th. At 5:00 AM, a formation of enemy aircraft in three squadrons approached from the Sea of Japan. An air raid alert was issued in preparation. By 6:00 AM, the enemy aircraft had successively approached the airspace over the Imperial Capital, Kawasaki City, and the port of Yokohama. The Japanese air defense air force, anti-aircraft artillery units, and 260,000 members of the air defense corps in the three cities began coordinated action to repel them. The air raid alert was lifted. At 8:00 AM, the Eastern Defense Commander and the mayors of Tokyo, Yokohama, and Kawasaki delivered words of gratitude via radio broadcast. Thus, the landmark joint air defense drill, lasting four nights and five days, concluded with great success. (Domei, 24th)

Travelogue of Japan (6) 65

— Our Reporter Hu Zhongchi, Hu Yizang

So he gave us several small books and printed materials, one of which was the Showa 10th edition of the "Kobe City Overview." In addition, there were beautifully printed materials compiled by the tourism section, such as "Kobe for Tourism," "Kobe Guide," "Historical Sites of the Genpei War," "Visiting Kobe Temples and Shrines," "Kobe City Picture Postcards," and so on. He pointed to the "Kobe City Overview" and said to us, "The Showa 11th edition is not yet printed. You can also find some materials regarding the city's finances in the roads section."

(Note) According to the Kobe City Overview, the Kobe City budget for the fiscal year of Showa 8 showed that under the revenue item, the city expenses belonging to the ordinary economy were more than 17.68 million yuan (Japanese yen), and those belonging to the special economy were more than 25.47 million Japanese yen. Under the expenditure item, regular expenses were more than 27.7 million yuan, and temporary expenses were more than 15.3 million yuan. The direct national tax and city tax borne by Kobe citizens in the fiscal year of Showa 8 increased compared to the fiscal year of 7. The average burden per person was 9 yuan and 50 sen for direct national tax, and 10 yuan and 65 sen for city tax, totaling 20 yuan and 15 sen.

We didn't want to ask anything else, so we thanked Secretary Kai and walked out of the city hall.

(5) Sakaemachi and Motomachi

In the afternoon, we wanted to visit the local newspaper offices, so we went to Sakaemachi. This is the financial center of Kobe, with stone and steel-reinforced concrete buildings standing one after another, mostly banks or companies. The two local tabloid newspapers in Kobe, Yushin Nippo and Kobe Shinkai, are also located there.

We went to Yushin Nippo first. We were received by Omi Kaname, a reporter from the social affairs department of the editorial bureau. Later, we went to Kobe Shimbun, where we were also received by a reporter from the social affairs department of the editorial bureau. The scale of both newspaper offices is not large. The former has a capital of 400,000 yuan (Japanese yen), and the president is named Takagi Kurakichi. The latter has a capital of 500,000 yuan, and the president is named Shindo Nobuyoshi. The internal organization is roughly the same. The entire company is divided into three bureaus: editorial, printing, and business. The editorial bureau is further divided into four departments: politics, economics, society, and art. All political news must be sent to the prefectural government for review every day. All the machinery in the printing bureau, including the printing cylinder, is domestically manufactured. The typesetters all wear black work clothes, and lighter tasks such as returning lead letters are the responsibility of female workers.

In the evening, Consul-General Jiang invited us to dinner at the Ginsui Western-style restaurant in Sakaemachi. The restaurant is located in the basement of a bank building. Going down the marble staircase, there is a large restaurant, decorated luxuriously, with valuable oil paintings hanging on the walls, and a fountain in the center. We first entered another lounge to chat with Consul-General Jiang and Vice-Consul Pan for a while, and then went to the restaurant for dinner. The host's hospitality, the elegance of the place, the abundance of dishes, and the attentive service of the beautiful waitresses made us feel infinite gratitude and pleasure.

After leaving the restaurant, we thanked Consuls Jiang and Pan and walked to Motomachi for sightseeing. This is one of the bustling centers of Kobe. The asphalt streets are not particularly wide, and there are no tram tracks running through them. Neat rows of lily-of-the-valley-style electric lights form countless brilliant arcs. It is said that the design of these streetlights was created by a professor of engineering in Japan. Various small Japanese-style shops are opened on both sides of the street, and there are also magnificent department stores and glamorous dance halls and cafes. On one section of the road, rows of stalls do business under their own gas lamps, adding to the liveliness of the city. We walked among crowds of people in various costumes, occasionally hearing the tunes of Japanese songs broadcast on the radio from both sides, and seeing young men on dates walking out of dance halls with dancers' arms in theirs, we couldn't help but feel a beautiful and exotic flavor in our hearts.

It was already past 10 o'clock when we returned to the hotel. Vice-Consul Pan knew that we would be going to Osaka tomorrow morning, so he came to the hotel late at night with Chen Deqi, the secretary of the consulate, to have a long talk with us. Thanks to their guidance, we gained a lot of convenience in our subsequent travels. We will never forget their kindness and teachings.

The Hebei-Chahar Political Council Adds Four Members; Cao Rulin Will Be Relied Upon for Diplomatic Issues; Mongolian Representatives Arrive in Beiping to Discuss the Current Situation in Inner Mongolia 66

Beiping Correspondence: From a superficial perspective, the situation in North China has been generally calm for the past month. Since the swift resolution of the so-called incident at Kakudai Dagu, the Hebei-Chahar authorities have been actively strengthening their internal affairs. Regarding personnel matters, concrete discussions were held when Wang Kemin came to Beiping. Wang also telegraphed Cao Rulin in Tianjin to come to Beiping for consultations. Cao stayed in Beiping for one night and then returned to Tianjin. As a result of the consultations, Song Zheyuan telegraphed Beijing to recommend Cao Rulin, Tang Erhe, Liu Ruming, and Ge Dingyuan as members of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council. The Executive Yuan approved this on the 21st. Cao was originally a diplomatic advisor to the council. All parties believe that the government will rely heavily on Cao in future diplomatic issues. Tang Erhe was invited to Tianjin when Wang Kemin arrived to seek his opinions. Tang is a senior alumnus of Japanese studies and was heavily relied upon when Huang Fu presided over the Political Affairs Reorganization Committee. His re-appointment this time is also based on trust. Liu Ruming, now the chairman of the Chahar Provincial Government, is naturally a member of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council. Ge Dingyuan was originally the secretary-general of the Political Council and has been trusted by Song and others since taking office. Although he is now a member of the council, Ge will continue to serve as secretary-general. It is reported that before the announcement of the four members, the list was finalized by Wang Kemin in Beiping and brought to Beijing by Wang for discussion and publication. After Yang Zhaogeng, the director of the Department of Civil Affairs of the Chahar Provincial Government, was transferred to the position of director of the Department of Political Affairs of the Political Council, he could not concurrently serve as the director of the Department. On the 21st, the council issued an order for Chairman Liu Ruming to concurrently serve as the director. Guo Zhihan, the director of the Department of Finance of Chahar Province, is now the director of the Department of Finance of the Political Council and finds it difficult to be responsible for the affairs of the Department of Finance of Chahar Province. At the same time, the council ordered Yang Mu, who was the director of the Ping-Sui Railway Bureau during the Northwest Army era, to act as the director. Zhang Yunrong succeeded as the Changlu Salt Transport Envoy, and Li Zishi succeeded as the Tianjin Customs Superintendent. Regarding diplomatic issues concerning "Eastern Hebei" and "Northern Chahar," although Itagaki and Tada had repeated consultations when they were in Beiping and Tianjin, they ultimately did not reach any results. Since Tashiro and Matsumuro took office, they have also contacted them several times, but the other party has refused to discuss the issues further, claiming that they want to change the political issues of Hebei and Chahar. As a result, the negotiations have stalled. Recently, Matsumuro has even said that there are no diplomatic issues to discuss in Hebei and Chahar, making it impossible to proceed. They can only let things take their natural course.

Regarding Inner Mongolia, the situation is not very clear. Representatives of Prince De have recently arrived in Beiping. According to the representatives, Prince De's environment in Mongolia is too harsh. Although there are many unclear rumors outside, he has never betrayed the central government and still hopes for a comprehensive solution to protect the border.

The Han River Continues to Rise; The Issue of Blocking the Breach of the Yaodi Embankment in Zhongxiang; Funding Needs Range from 800,000 to 2 Million Yuan; Qin Fen Flies from Beijing to Wuhan to Inspect Shagang 67

Hankou Correspondence: After the continuous breaches of the Yaodi Embankment in Zhongxiang, the waters of the Xiang River have been rising excessively, threatening the lives of citizens in eleven counties and cities, including Zhongxiang, Jingmen, Tianmen, and Hanchuan. When the embankment was repaired by the Xiang Embankment Engineering Office, it already cost 2.7 million yuan. During the period when the Disaster Relief Committee was blocking the breach, it cost another 300,000 yuan, totaling more than 3 million yuan. Now, if they want to rebuild it, not only is the project huge and time is tight, but also the funding is difficult to raise. If they postpone construction, they will sit idly by while the citizens of eleven counties are submerged. The government is in a situation where it wants to act but cannot, and wants to stop but cannot. The responsible personnel are also trapped in a dilemma.范熙績, the director of the Disaster Relief Committee, previously convened a meeting. After careful study by various engineering experts, they summarized four proposals: (1) Shi Dupei, the chief engineer of the Jianghan Engineering Bureau, proposed to block the original breach with 8,000 cubic meters of boulders to close the gap, with the addition of riprap dams and diversion channels, requiring a total of 1.45 million yuan; (2) Chen Ruzhen, a commissioner of the Economic Commission, proposed to use the gabion method to build double dams inside and outside the original breach to close the gap, using thorny branches as the main material, along with ancillary works, requiring more than 1.9 million yuan; (3) Yang Silian and Wang Zhang, commissioners of the provincial government, proposed to build a crescent embankment outside the original breach, using the old method of driving piles, making mud sweeps, and throwing boulders to close the gap, requiring 880,000 yuan including ancillary works; (4) Another proposal was to abandon blocking the breach during the flood season and wait until autumn to first block the original dam at Xiongjia Bridge, so that the Yaodi breach would dry up, and then block the breach, also requiring more than 800,000 yuan including ancillary works. Among the above four items, the first item was absolutely impossible to adopt because the time to purchase and transport the boulders was too long. The second item required too much funding, and the time was not economical. The third item was the fastest and the cost was lower than the first two, but the risk was greater. The fourth item required the least funding and was the most stable, but it could not be carried out at this time. As a result, the discussions were divided, and no agreement was reached. The project was increasingly stalled. Qin Fen, the secretary-general of the committee, specially took a plane from Beijing to Wuhan with water conservancy expert Pu Deli on the 21st. He exchanged views with Lu Zhu, the secretary-general of the provincial government, and Liu Shupeng, the director of the Department of Construction. He then took a special boat to Shagang Embankment to inspect the breach and discussed everything in detail with Fan Xiji before returning to Wuhan to meet with Yang Yongtai, the chairman of the provincial government. What method will be adopted will have to wait for the final decision of Yang and Qin. (July 21)

Financial Stability Gradually Achieved in Sichuan Province; Local Currency Disappears, Exchange Rates Decrease; Promotion of the New Currency Balances Prices 68

Chengdu Correspondence: Since the Central Bank established branches in Chengdu and Chongqing and offices in Wanxian and Santai to make every effort to adjust, the financial situation in Sichuan Province has gradually stabilized. Local newspapers do not have detailed records. The general outline is recorded as follows:

Suppressing Exchange Rates: Before the Central Bank established branches in Chengdu and Chongqing, the exchange rates for foreign currency in the two places were alarmingly high. The highest rate was 440 yuan of exchange rate for every 1,000 yuan exchanged for Shanghai currency. The exchange rates fluctuated constantly, and unscrupulous merchants took the opportunity to manipulate them. Legitimate merchants suffered great losses when purchasing and transporting goods. After the Central Bank implemented the method of equal exchange rates, the exchange between Sichuan and Shanghai became very convenient and inexpensive. As a result, the exchange of foreign currency in Sichuan Province became extremely convenient, and the commercial transportation between Sichuan and Shanghai gradually recovered to its past prosperity.

Recalling and Destroying Local Currency: The former Sichuan Local Bank issued 30 million yuan in banknotes. Because they were issued in Chongqing, the markets in Chengdu referred to them as Chongqing currency or local currency. Their prices also fluctuated like the exchange rates in the past, sometimes rising to more than 90% and sometimes falling to more than 60%. The lives of ordinary people were unstable. After the Chairman's Headquarters resolutely decided to issue an order to recall and destroy local currency at 80% of the legal currency or 100% of the local currency, the Sichuan Provincial Government borrowed 24 million yuan of legal currency with financial bonds to entrust the two branches of the Central Bank to successively recall 30 million yuan of local currency. It was recalled and destroyed in succession. By the end of last year, local currency had disappeared from the markets in Sichuan Province.

Promoting Legal Currency: When the national government promulgated the new currency policy, prices in Shanghai and Hankou rose slightly, but the markets in Sichuan Province were not affected. The reason was that the Central Bank clearly stipulated methods to eliminate exchange rates and uniformly exchange currency. The Chengdu and Chongqing branches collected and delivered legal currency in general. Merchants in the two cities, who had suffered from high exchange rates, were relieved of a heavy burden and were happy to use legal currency for foreign exchange. Those who did not have legal currency purchased it with cash. At that time, it required 120 yuan in cash in the Chengdu market to purchase 100 yuan of legal currency. Therefore, legal currency could be circulated in Sichuan. Later, because the Central Bank followed orders and allowed various banks to use 60% of cash and 40% of public bonds to receive 100% of legal currency, various banks competed to purchase cash. As a result, the price of legal currency slightly decreased, and the banks benefited greatly from this banknote subsidy. As a result, finance became more stable.

Issuing Subsidiary Currency: Sichuan Province had the most subsidiary currency coins, the worst quality, and the most types in the country. Later, because unscrupulous merchants manipulated and ignorant villagers hoarded copper coins, bad coins became scarce commodities. In April and May of this year, one yuan of legal currency could only be exchanged for 18,000 copper coins, and it was not easy to obtain. All the money shops removed their currency exchange signs. Exchanging currency required personal connections. For a time, the city and suburbs felt quite panic. By June, the copper-nickel subsidiary coins minted by the Central Mint were transported to Sichuan Province, first issued in Chongqing, and then successively transported to Chengdu. The total amount was more than 1 million yuan, gradually spreading throughout society. As a result, the difficulty of exchanging legal currency was completely eliminated. From then on, currency prices never rose or fell, and commodity prices were balanced. However, the old and inferior copper coins cast in Sichuan Province are still circulating in the market, and the people are suffering. It is hoped that the government will issue a clear order to abolish all the old and inferior copper coins and order the government to recall and recast them within a limited time. At the same time, the Central Bank should continue to transport copper-nickel subsidiary currency to Sichuan to regulate the market. If so, the chaotic currency system problem in Sichuan Province for many years can be thoroughly resolved, and the people's livelihood can be stabilized.

Dispute Over Training of Faculty and Staff in Middle Schools in Hubei; The Department of Education Is Determined to Maintain Its Authority; Teachers Refuse to Accept in Order to Preserve Their Dignity 69

Hankou Correspondence: The educational circles in Hubei Province often experienced turmoil in the past few years, but have calmed down in recent years. The teaching results have indeed made significant progress. However, this year's summer vacation, all public and private middle school faculty and staff in the province held lectures. The Department of Education ordered the addition of a concentrated training program, from August 3 to 28, as a period of military management. Those who did not receive training would have their qualifications as faculty and staff revoked, which led to disputes. The Department of Education stated in a letter that it was determined to maintain its authority. The teachers, on the other hand, refused to accept in order to preserve their dignity. Although they have not yet gone to extremes, it is difficult to resolve the issue immediately. Cheng Qibao, the director of the Department of Education, specially issued a letter to the faculty and staff, and the faculty and staff also published a notice in the newspaper. More than 40 faculty and staff representatives held a discussion meeting at the YMCA in Wuhan City today (23rd) to discuss how to deal with the situation and to entertain reporters and report on the progress of the situation. It can be seen that this matter has not yet found a solution. The main points of Cheng Qibao's letter to the faculty and staff and the report of the faculty and staff are recorded as follows:

Cheng Qibao's Letter to Faculty and Staff

In summary, the methods set for this session of the lecture are aimed at refining the spirit of colleagues, improving the atmosphere of the education community. At the beginning of the establishment, it was inevitable that the rope would be tightened too strictly. All those who can find ways to improve have been revised again and again. The time period has been extended, and the technical subjects are only 50 minutes each day, and the training is divided into groups in consideration of physical strength and age. Other matters such as food, accommodation, rescue, and hygiene are also well planned within the scope of possibility. If it is still said that the physical strength is still not up to par, it is difficult to believe. Recalling the summer of the 23rd year, the summer lecture for elementary schools also adopted a group living method. At that time, the weather was hot and the equipment was lacking, far exceeding this lecture. However, the elementary school faculty and staff who participated were energetic and initially did not hear anyone reporting that they were in pain. Middle school teachers occupy a very important position in society. At this time, when the country is in trouble, saving the country is an important task and cannot be shirked. They should follow President Chiang Kai-shek's instructions to work hard and move forward, exercise their bodies, and encourage the people. From any point of view, there should be no doubt. Moreover, the lecture is an important policy decided by the government, and the method has been announced long ago and is bound to be implemented. If you cannot understand this intention and cause obstacles, how will you serve as an example to society and supervise students in the future? And the government will never turn a blind eye to this. I hope you will understand this intention well and participate enthusiastically.

Faculty and Staff Representatives State Their Position

Faculty and staff representatives reported the progress of the matter to reporters today and stated their position. Zhang Huiwu, Xia Bochu, and Wang Shunqing spoke in succession, expressing their absolute support for the principle of centralized training. The Department of Education has clearly stipulated summer academic lectures, and faculty and staff have actively participated in previous summer lectures. The government can carry out centralized training of faculty and staff at any time in the future. Why must it be during the short summer vacation, and there should be no regulation that those who do not receive training will not be certified? This move would wipe out the qualifications that faculty and staff have obtained over many years from elementary school to university. Moreover, the teachers' petitions have not been approved by the authorities, and it is not known how much the content has been improved. It is hoped that the authorities will respect the personality of the education community. In addition, it is also necessary to study the reform of middle schools in fact. The number of hours undertaken by class instructors is equal to that of full-time teachers. With more than a dozen classes of students in middle schools, it is difficult for one instructor to guide and manage internal affairs with their energy. (July 23)

Full Through Traffic on the Guangdong-Hankou Railway to Open Soon; The Railway Bureau Is Scheduled to Establish Offices in Guangdong and Hankou; Ling Hongxun and Zhou Zhongqi Will Serve as Director and Deputy Director Respectively 70

Hankou Correspondence: The opening of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, which the whole country has been looking forward to, was originally scheduled to be realized, but it has been delayed until now due to the situation in Guangdong and Guangxi. Now that Chen Jitang has been forced to go to Hong Kong, the situation has taken a sharp turn for the worse. The call for the opening of the entire line has been revived. Although the two steel bridges at Jiufeng and Tiantoushui in the southern section were destroyed by the military, it is not enough to hinder progress. The Ministry of Railways believes that the construction of the Zhushao section has been completed and is actively planning for direct through traffic on the entire line. All the management bureaus of the Xiang-E and Guang-Shao sections and the engineering bureau of the Zhushao section should be merged and organized under one authority. An order has been issued by the ministry on the 21st to reorganize into the "Guangdong-Hankou Railway Administration," and Ling Hongxun and Zhou Zhongqi have been appointed as the director and deputy director of the bureau. The organizational regulations have also been issued with the order. The three bureaus will be merged and reorganized, and the bureau headquarters will be located in Xujiapeng, Wuchang. It is scheduled to be formally established on August 1. The organizational system takes the Railway Administration as the highest management authority of the entire line. Under the director and deputy director, there are six departments: Secretariat, General Affairs, Transportation, Business, Engineering, Factory Affairs, and Accounting. The candidates for the Secretary and the heads of each department have also been internally determined. The General Affairs Department has jurisdiction over six sections: (1) Documents Section, (2) Personnel Section, (3) Materials Section, Materials Factory, (4) Industry Section, (5) Health Section, (6) Affairs Section. The Transportation Department has jurisdiction over five sections: (1) Operations Section, (2) Telecommunications Section, (3) Mechanical Engineering Section, (4) Accounting Section, (5) Transportation Section, Transportation Station. The Business Department has jurisdiction over three sections: (1) Passenger Section, (2) Freight Section, (3) Business Section. The Engineering Department has jurisdiction over three sections: (1) Construction Section, (2) Design Section, (3) Engineering Section, Engineering Sub-section. The Factory Affairs Department has jurisdiction over three sections: (1) Management Section, (2) Technical Section, (3) Machine Factory and the Guangdong Office, the Hankou Office. The Accounting Department has jurisdiction over three sections: (1) General Audit Section, (2) Inspection Section, (3) Cashier Section. Ling, who was concurrently the director of the Xiang-E sections of the Zhushao headquarters, had previously requested to return to Hankou from Beijing. It is reported that he has gone to Hengzhou again to make arrangements. The opening of the entire line will not be far off. (July 21)

Suzhou Tax Reduction on Soybean Cakes Denied 72

The soybean cake industry in Suzhou, Wuxi, Changshu, Kunshan, and other places previously applied to the ministry and provincial authorities for a tax reduction because the business tax rate levied on the industry was originally 0.2%, but later increased to 0.5%. At a time when commerce is declining, the burden is really unbearable, so they have repeatedly striven to reduce the tax to 0.2% in order to maintain commerce, etc. The Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce also submitted an application to the ministry for a tax reduction for this issue. The Ministry of Industry has now issued an order saying, "After investigation, this case was previously submitted to the ministry by the Jiangsu Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce based on the association's letters and telegrams. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has been consulted regarding the case of Jiangsu Province levying an additional business tax on the soybean cake industry. The Jiangnan Soybean Cake Industry Association has requested the Jiangsu Provincial Government for a response. According to the regulations, the soybean cake industry should not be levied at 0.5%. It is now handled in accordance with the regulations and there is no additional increase. Please know that your request should not be discussed," etc. The County Chamber of Commerce often immediately forwarded the order to the industry association to inform them.

New President of the Guangdong High Court, Ye Xiasheng, Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday; Discusses Four Major Plans to Rectify the Judiciary in Guangdong Province; Will Take a Steamer on the 25th to Guangdong to Assume Office 76

At 8:00 PM that evening, prominent figures from Guangdong residing in Shanghai and lawyers Feng Bingnan, Wu Chengyu, Zai Siji, Cao Daozhi, etc., jointly hosted a banquet at the New Asia Hotel. Ye is scheduled to take the French mail ship General Joffre this morning to return south. The ship arrived in Shanghai from Japan yesterday afternoon and berthed at the Osaka Wharf in Yangshupu. It is scheduled to depart south at 11:00 AM sharp.

Ye's Remarks

A reporter from the Central News Agency met with Ye at the station and asked about the issue of reorganizing the judiciary in Guangdong Province. According to him, during the Guangdong Restoration of 1911, he served as the Minister of Justice in Guangdong. At that time, he was young and had little time. He went to Beijing to work for the Provisional Government, so he had no suggestions. When Premier Sun Yat-sen went south to uphold the constitution in 1917, the Minister of Interior, concurrently managing judicial administration, was the current President Ju of the Judicial Yuan. He was then Deputy Minister. At that time, the Gui clique occupied Guangdong, and everything was obstructed, the judiciary was dark, and the people suffered. Premier Sun Yat-sen ordered him to lead eight soldiers to take over the four judicial bureaus. Mo Rongxin was furious and surrounded the court with two battalions of soldiers all day long, but could do nothing about Premier Sun Yat-sen. He followed the instructions of Minister Ju and made major rectifications. The people were delighted and called Premier Sun Yat-sen the "Blue Sky," and the affection still remains today. The good laws and intentions have been followed without interruption. Unfortunately, it only lasted four months, and the Marshal's Office was forced to disperse by the warlords. Although Premier Sun Yat-sen later re-established his government in Guangdong, the constant warfare made it impossible to take care of it. Over the past ten years, the accumulated malpractices have deepened. This time, with the Guangdong situation stabilized, the Central Government complied with public opinion, and the two presidents of the Judicial Yuan and the Ministry of Judicial Administration considered him to be a guide and assigned him this task. He believed that since the Northern Expedition, he had been living off his savings and had no intention of asking about politics. However, seeing the Guangdong people suffer under the tyrannical government year after year, all attributed to the poor judiciary, he, out of a sense of urgent concern for his homeland and compassion for the people, became Feng Fu again. The mandates he received from the Central Government are: (1) to close the Southwest Branch Court, (2) to rectify the discipline of the legal profession, (3) to eliminate poverty, corruption, and long-standing malpractices, and (4) to seek convenience for the public. Although he is not talented, he firmly believes that his two colleagues, Xie Yingbo and Du Zhiqiu, who have also been entrusted by the Central Government, will be able to understand the virtues of the Judicial Yuan and the Ministry of Judicial Administration, implement the people-saving proposals, and serve as loyal servants for their hometown.

Zhejiang Provincial Association Held a Board Meeting Yesterday 88

The Zhejiang Provincial Association convened a meeting of the standing directors at its meeting place in Lianzhuli, Avenue Evigny, at 5:00 PM yesterday, chaired by Chu Huiseng. The formalities were carried out as usual. First, the chairman reported the purpose of today's meeting: one was for Mr. He Zhongliu to state the matters of the bandit police in eastern Zhejiang, and the other was for the Dai Mountain massacre. Discussing Zhejiang affairs in Zhejiang, the association should make some expression. The results of the discussion: (1) Regarding the Dai Mountain massacre, according to those who came to Shanghai from Dai Mountain to state the details, the case was actually initiated by the mountain tax police. The salt farmers' request to postpone the returning of the salt mounds was not inappropriate. A quarrel with a surveyor started the conflict. The tax police immediately dispatched a large armed police force to fire warning shots, killing several salt farmers. As a result, the fishermen took the opportunity to form a team to resist and vent their anger, resulting in the tragic case of killing officials, destroying bureaus, and strangling many people. It was decided to handle this case separately. Regarding the salt farmers, the government's salt transport envoy and commissioner's office should be notified by telegram to investigate the victimized salt farmers and provide appropriate compensation. The fleeing salt farmers should be persuaded to return to their hometowns and resume their businesses, and the manufacturers should be supervised to prepare funds for reopening the salt fields at the same time. As for the returning of the salt mounds and the purchase of land, the price must be paid according to the value, and no arbitrary occupation is allowed. The tax police captain who caused the trouble should be severely punished. Regarding the fishermen, their usual hardships should be stated, such as the discoloration of the salt, rain, and water stains. If the color is slightly lighter, it must be punished and confiscated. The confiscated salt can be freely sold by the tax police after paying taxes. In the past, a single was issued once a year. Before the single was exhausted, the stored salt was also considered private salt and confiscated. Fishing must take advantage of the tide. In the past, it was customary to issue a single at night, but now it is stipulated that the office must check the points. If the time is missed, the single cannot be issued to go to sea, and the fishermen's losses are even greater. As for the fish, after it has discolored, whether red or black, it is not easy to be welcomed by customers. If used as substitute for bran, the tax police believe that it can be mixed with edible salt after being screened. If rice bran is used, the fish will be easily moldy and rotten due to heavy steaming. In the past, the National Federation of Commerce and Industry requested the salt affairs officials in Shandong to find ways to improve the situation, and the result was a temporary suspension. The above matters should be submitted to the Salt Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of Finance for review and handling. After the discussion, the meeting adjourned at around 6:00 PM. The villagers of Jinhua have moved to the city in droves. We are sending a telegram to implore Your Excellency to quickly dispatch strong troops to suppress the bandits and appease the people. The Shanghai Zhejiang Provincial Association bows.

President of the Chinese Overseas Community in Honolulu, Zhuo Lin, Returns to China and Arrives in Shanghai; Interviews the Facts of the Honolulu Dam 89

The Honolulu Dam is a water barrier on the Jinghui Canal in Shaanxi, which raises and maintains the water level of the Jing River at a certain height during normal and low water levels, so as to contain water into the canal. The dam site is located upstream of the Old Dragon King Temple, at the old canal entrance of Guanghui, made of cement, with a top height of 68 meters, a top width of 5 meters, and a maximum depth of 9.2 meters. The stonework volume is 4,413.6 cubic feet. In 1930, there was a severe drought in North China, and the land was barren for thousands of miles. The China International Famine Relief Commission proposed organizing work relief and opening up the Jinghui Canal to save the people and benefit irrigation. The Shaanxi Provincial Government strongly supported its success and cooperated with it. The Honolulu Chinese General Chamber of Commerce then rose up to assist in raising donations to help achieve this goal. It successively contributed 145,000 yuan in national currency. The Famine Relief Commission specially allocated this amount to build the water barrier dam. In order to leave a permanent memorial, it was named Honolulu. Construction began in the summer of 1931 and was completed in June of the following year. It faces the Zhu Zibeike Two Bridges from a distance and is sufficient for thousands of years. The Honolulu Chinese Overseas Community in Honolulu published the second collection of "Honolulu Overseas Chinese" this year, naming it after the dam, which is a credit to the overseas Chinese in Honolulu. It is planned to interview the detailed construction process and publish it in order to leave a record. The president of the community, Zhuo Lin, returned to Shanghai on the President Coolidge ocean liner the day before yesterday and specially inquired about the details from the Chinese Foreign Relief Commission. An Xianjin, the executive committee member of the commission, and others warmly entertained him, hosted a banquet, and presented him with photos of the dam and explanations in Chinese and English. It is heard that Zhuo Jun was very happy to obtain this good material.

Shanghai's real estate industry has been affected by the global economic recession, resulting in a sharp drop in prices and the disappearance of transactions. A special letter was sent to the banking industry and the money industry to jointly petition the Ministry of Finance for remedial measures. The banking industry and the money industry have now separately studied the legal issues. After the study is completed, they will jointly consult and submit a report to the Ministry for review and handling. Motion to Restrict Artificial Silk Imports; Ministry of Finance Replied that it Should be Discussed Later; In the Current Situation, the Focus is on Investigating Smuggled Goods, Not on Restrictions 94

The Shanghai China National Products Maintenance Association previously petitioned the Ministry of Finance to order the promotion of domestic goods and the establishment of artificial silk factories, and to gradually prohibit the import of artificial silk. Yesterday, a telegram was received from the Ministry of Finance stating that the China National Products Maintenance Association's application has been received. This case has been forwarded to the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan and distributed to the two ministries. The request to promote the use of domestic goods and establish artificial silk factories is under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Industry, and should be reviewed and handled by the two ministries. As for the request to gradually restrict the quantity of imported artificial silk and other textiles and gradually prohibit them, this Ministry has thoroughly investigated. According to customs records, the imported value of artificial silk and other textiles, artificial silk satin, and artificial silk-interwoven textiles, as well as artificial silk-interwoven wool and cotton textiles, totaled more than 690,000 yuan in 1933, and only more than 390,000 yuan in 1934. This shows that since the import tax rate on artificial silk and other textiles has been increased, the normal import volume has been sharply reduced, and there is no need to restrict it again. As for the tax-evading artificial silk and other textiles in North China, new regulations for punishing tax evasion and regulations for inspection and distribution have been newly formulated, and inspection offices have been established on various railways to order serious investigation and strict implementation. The finished products woven from artificial silk have been stipulated to be included in the list of items to be inspected. In the future, the trend of smuggling will gradually subside, and the volume of imports should be reduced. Therefore, from the current situation, the focus on imported artificial silk and other textiles is on investigating smuggled goods, not on restrictions. The request to restrict and prohibit should be discussed later. In addition to replying to the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan, this telegram is sent for your information. Ministry of Finance.

Ministry of Railways Unifies Joint Transportation Methods for Various Routes, Stipulating Five Items for Compliance 97

The Ministry of Railways, noting inconsistencies in the methods for handling joint transportation of goods across various routes, which caused difficulties for local railway bureaus in managing this business, has selected key aspects of joint transportation and stipulated five unified methods. These are to be implemented uniformly across all routes. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, upon receiving the order to comply with the aforementioned methods, have instructed their respective traffic departments to follow them. The details of these methods are as follows: 1. The method of payment for joint transportation of goods, whether in full carloads or less-than-carload lots, shall be uniformly handled. 2. Actively implement methods for collecting payment on behalf of others for goods. 3. When joint transportation of educational materials is offered, the special price for educational materials prescribed by the Ministry should be applied using the long-distance reduction method for joint transportation. 4. For sixth-class goods and goods with freight rates equal to or lower than sixth-class, with the exception of those stipulated in Article 7 of the General Rules for Freight Transportation, which may not be handled with guaranteed joint transportation, and with the temporary exception of coal, coke, ash, and slag, all other goods should be handled with guaranteed joint transportation. 5. Railway stations should uniformly implement the practice of issuing receipts for guaranteed joint transportation of goods on behalf of other routes.

Should Union Dues Receipts Have Revenue Stamps Affixed? General Labor Union Petitions for Interpretation 100

According to Da Gong She, the Municipal General Labor Union yesterday submitted petitions to the Legislative Yuan, the Judicial Yuan, the Ministry of Industry, and the Ministry of Finance stating: "The Members' Dyeing Trade Union, a subordinate association, reported that the revenue authority's inspectors considered receipts for monthly dues paid by all workers of the Ruihe Factory lacking revenue stamps, and filed a lawsuit in the Shanghai District Court. The subordinate association, upon receiving the summons, based on Article 34 of the Public Association Law, 'Public associations are exempt from income tax, business tax, and registration tax,' and Article 3, paragraph 3 of the General Rules of the Stamp Tax Law, 'Vouchers issued by government agencies or autonomous organizations for handling public funds or public money,' and paragraph 8 ('Documents used internally by public or private organizations that do not create external rights or obligations'), various provisions, dispatched personnel to the court to argue the case and also petitioned the relevant authorities and requested the court to suspend the case and also requested the central government to give an interpretation. The Shanghai District Court misinterpreted the articles and, before the Central government has given an interpretation, arbitrarily imposed a fine of nine yuan through a criminal ruling. This action by the court not only distorts central laws but also affects the entire union economy. It is appropriate to petition the relevant authorities to sue the court and request the legislative authority to give an interpretation with clear stipulations for compliance." According to the above, Article 34 of the Public Association Law stipulates: "Public associations are exempt from income tax, business tax, and registration tax," and Article 3, paragraph 3 of the Stamp Tax Law stipulates: "Vouchers issued by government agencies or autonomous organizations for handling public funds or public money," and paragraph 8 of the same article stipulates: "Documents used internally by public or private organizations that do not create external rights or obligations," all have provisions for exemption from stamp tax. Since the public association is an autonomous organization of workers, its dues receipts are vouchers issued for handling public money, and there is no doubt that they are exempt from stamp tax. Moreover, the dues receipts do not create external rights or obligations, and according to the Stamp Tax Law, they are even more obviously exempt. Furthermore, according to the provisions of item 4 of the tax rate table in Article 16 of the Stamp Tax Law, "Vouchers or ledgers issued by public enterprises for taking or remitting money, or public ledgers used by workers in various industries to withdraw wages, are exempt from stamp tax." Since public ledgers used by workers to withdraw wages are exempt from stamp tax, it is inappropriate to classify union dues receipts as money or goods receipts under item 2 of Article 16 of the Stamp Tax Law and impose a fine. The case involves national laws and regulations and the union economy, and is of utmost importance. Therefore, this petition is submitted to your (Yuan) (Ministry) for interpretation to facilitate compliance.

Workers at Shenfeng Dyeing Factory Went on Strike Last Night 101

According to Da Gong She, the Shenfeng Dyeing Factory, located at No. 200 Huangyu Road at the end of Yinxiang Port in this city, was established in the autumn of the year before last. It has only a few dozen workers and is not very large in scale. The factory owner, Chen Shaoji, also serves as the manager. The workers' wages have always been meager, relying entirely on wine money. The wine money is divided according to a ratio of four for the workers and six for the factory, after the workers are paid a fixed salary. The remaining 40% of the wine money belongs to the factory owner. However, the factory suddenly deducted another 20% from the workers' wine money as savings without providing workers' savings certificates. Moreover, when business reached more than 10,000 pieces, the wages of all workers were deducted, and they were only given wine money. The workers have suffered deeply. Recently, the workers, unable to endure the factory's oppression, requested mediation from party and government agencies, demanding improved treatment. However, the factory owner ignored them completely. Unable to find any other means, the workers went on strike together yesterday (the 24th). Several workers were guarding the factory gate, and the order was still good. They are now waiting for party and government agencies to mediate.

Zhejiang Cocoon Association Submits to Zhejiang Provincial Government: Request for Eye-Witness Review of Cocoon Reeling Deduction; Public Interest Yong Cocoon's Poor Quality Deduction Disparate from Hangzhou Factory Reeling Deduction 102

The Zhejiang Cocoon Industry Association Federation of Lianzhu Lane, Aiwenyi Road, this city, submitted a document to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting an on-site review of cocoon reeling deduction by original cocoon farmers to ensure accuracy. The Public Interest Yong Cocoon Firm stated in its letter: "We received the Zhejiang.

Silk Control Committee's Sixth District Receipt Office Notice No. 12, which stated: 'On July 16th of this year, we received Instruction No. 2048 from the Zhejiang Provincial Silk Control Committee, which stated: 'After investigation, the cocoon samples submitted by the district that did not meet the central price have been test-reeled by our Hangzhou Silk Factory. It has been determined that the Liu family cocoon firms, including Tiancheng, Xianghe, Public Interest, Xiangxi, Hengchang, and Tonghe, should be punished separately. We hereby send a copy of the reeling deduction table for each firm and order you to comply and execute the order and report the compliance situation for verification.' We are sending this notice in addition to separate notices to the firms. The cocoon firms are ordered to quickly pay the fines in full within five days and submit them here for transfer, without delay, to avoid subsequent follow-up and tracking. This notice includes Public Interest Yong Cocoon Firm's selection deduction of 78.40, light deduction of 424.18.33, specified central price of 20.00, difference per dan of 1.77, total cocoons received of 1807.61, and fine amount of 6398.94, etc.' After investigation, the spring cocoons received by Public Interest Yong this year were of poor quality and had been test-reeled by the Shanghai Beautiful Silk Factory, with a light deduction of 508.0, which is greatly different from the Hangzhou Factory's reeling deduction, with a difference of 84.02. Public Interest Yong is located in the Linshang District of South Lake, and the

spring cocoons collected over the years have a reeling deduction of more than 600 catties. This year's cocoons are compressed and of low quality, so it is unusual that the reeling deduction is superior to the previous years. There must be errors in the reeling assessment. Moreover, the spring cocoons are still sealed and stored in the Shanghai Beautiful Silk Factory (untouched). Therefore, we request that your company forward this letter to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, ordering the Control Committee to send personnel to the Beautiful Silk Factory to retrieve samples for re-reeling to determine the accurate deduction. Only then can we be convinced whether a fine should be imposed. Attached is a reeling list from the Beautiful Silk Factory, please review it in detail to assist in the matter. On this basis, the Hangzhou Silk Factory and the Beautiful Silk Factory's test reeling of the cocoons of the Public Interest Yong Cocoon Firm has a large difference in reeling deduction, so it is necessary to retrieve samples for re-reeling. Our Silk Factory's test reeling

cannot be considered definitive. Often, the reeling deduction of the same cocoon firm's cocoons by the same silk factory is inconsistent. Only after all the cocoons have been reeled can the exact number of deductions be obtained. Now that the Hangzhou Silk Factory's test reeling is not limited to the original cocoon farmers and is only a one-time reeling, how can it be credible? Our Association believes that there are no regulations in this spring cocoon collection method that prescribe penalties for those below the central price. Arbitrary punishments after the fact seem inappropriate. Even if we take a step back, this test reeling is related to fines and should be conducted with the original cocoon farmers present to avoid criticism. It is also appropriate to choose two or more reputable silk factories to test reel simultaneously. Even if the accurate reeling deduction cannot be obtained, it will at least show fairness. This is our association's opinion. We respectfully submit this document to your government requesting the Control Committee to handle the matter according to this method. Only then can the Public Interest Yong Cocoon Firm review the deduction with their own eyes. We respectfully submit this to the Zhejiang Provincial Government (attached is a reeling list)."

Zhang Xiuying, a Woman from Beiping, is Deceived into Coming to Shanghai and Rescued 106

According to Da Tong She, Zhang Xiuying, a 19-year-old woman from Ningbo who resided in Beiping, was deceived into coming to Shanghai for medical treatment and was in danger of becoming destitute. Yesterday, she was sent to the China Women and Children Relief Association by the Ningbo Fellow-Countrymen Association in Shanghai for temporary care and to inform her family to come to Shanghai to claim her. The matter was quite tortuous, showing how treacherous people's hearts can be. The details are as follows. A Pitiful Background: The deceived woman was said to be educated and had studied in a certain elementary school in Shanghai before the Shanghai Incident, so her writing is quite clear. According to her account, her name is Zhang Xiuying, she is 19 years old, and is from Ningbo. When she was six years old, she was given up by her biological parents and adopted by Zhang Shougen, a fellow villager, as his stepdaughter (Zhang is a merchant in Tianjin). Soon after, she came to Shanghai with her stepmother, Zhang Wang, and lived at No. 3 Mingde Lane, Malong Road. At that time, her stepmother funded her education. However, after the Shanghai Incident broke out, she returned to her hometown in Ningbo with her stepmother. Deceived into Coming to Shanghai: On March 16th of this year, her stepfather took his family to live at No. 17 Julian Hutong, Beiping. However, she has been suffering from scrofula recently, and has not been cured since residing in Beiping. Unexpectedly, a neighbor woman from her time in Shanghai (whom she calls Auntie, name unknown), who had been close to her stepmother, recently sent a letter to Beiping saying that there was a specialized doctor in Shanghai who treated scrofula very effectively, and that if she wanted to be treated, the neighbor woman could come to Beiping to accompany her daughter to Shanghai for treatment. Her stepmother believed her, so the neighbor woman came to Beiping at the beginning of the month to accompany her to Shanghai for treatment.

Never to Return

On the way, the neighbor woman took away the 120 yuan in cash and the jewelry she had brought with her in the name of protecting them. By the time they arrived in Shanghai, the woman took her to see a front-facing room at No. 7 Ciai Lane, Xiaoshadu Road, agreed to a rent of ten yuan, and paid a deposit of one yuan. That afternoon, around 7:30 PM, the woman went out on the pretext of finding a doctor and never returned. Only then did she realize she had been deceived and began to cry loudly. After learning the details from the landlord, the landlord also wanted to force her out of the house. Just when she was at her wits' end, she suddenly remembered that she had a classmate named Wang Aizhen when she was studying in Shanghai, and heard that she was studying at an egg factory, but did not know the name of the factory.

Saved in Dire Straits

After inquiring, she learned that there was a Maochang Egg Factory on Huangpu Road, so she hired a car and went straight to the factory to inquire, and recounted her experiences. The factory staff, Jin Shaonan, etc., took pity on the young woman and the unfortunate situation, and sent someone to accompany her to the Ningbo Fellow-Countrymen Association in Shanghai and sent a letter to the association, saying: "Dear Sirs, Zhang Xiuying, a woman from Ningbo, residing in Beiping, came to Shanghai to treat scrofula and was deceived by her aunt out of her money and jewelry, and is now destitute on the sea, homeless. We respectfully request that your association inform the Fellow-Countrymen Association in Beiping to have her family come to claim her, so that the family can be reunited. We are deeply grateful. Sincerely, Jin Shaonan, Wang Hengtong, Zhang Xuming, Sun Wenheng."

Sent to Women and Children Relief Association

After learning the situation, the association sent another letter to the Fellow-Countrymen Association in Beiping to inform her family. The woman was sent to the China Women and Children Relief Association for temporary care. The letter to the Women and Children Relief Association stated: "Dear Sirs, Zhang Xiuying, a woman from Ningbo, resides with her parents in Beiping. This time, she was deceived by her aunt into coming to Shanghai to treat scrofula, and all the money and jewelry she brought with her were taken away, leaving her stranded in Shanghai, with no way to return home. We are sending the woman under escort, and request that your association take her in for temporary care. All expenses for food and lodging will be covered by our association. Please approve this request.

Guo Bingwen Details International Trade and the Situation of Overseas Chinese: Our Country's Main Exports to the U.S. Face Year-by-Year Tariff Reductions, The Overseas Chinese Commerce in Many Places Wanes and Appears Desolate, The U.S. Awards and Protection of Industry Can be Borrowed 107

Guo Bingwen, Director of the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, who was appointed by the government to go to the United States with Mr. Chen Guangfu to discuss the silver issue and investigate economic conditions in various places, reported on the situation of international trade in Europe and the United States and the recent situation of overseas Chinese in various places at the meeting of the Local Association on the 21st evening. These are all important current issues, and the reporter of Da Gong She has recorded them for the reference of those who are concerned about international trade and the situation of overseas Chinese.

The mission abroad for international trade and the process of contacting various parties have already been reported in the press. Originally, I (Guo himself) planned to investigate the local economic situation in Washington, but since I was going to New York a week later, I did not have time to go into detail. I will tell you (Guo said) about the process of contact and what is most relevant to international trade and China. When we were abroad, Japanese newspapers reported that we were buying arms, which was unfounded. Regarding trade between China and the United States, it has plummeted this year. Our country's bronzeware and antiques imported into the United States accounted for 50% of the percentage two years ago, but by last year, it suddenly dropped to 2%. Tea dropped from 39% to 6%. The export of tung oil was more than 30 million yuan last year due to the development and widespread use of the U.S. industry. However, due to the unevenness of the quality, the purchasing power of the United States gradually decreased, and Japanese oil took the opportunity to dump it on the market. According to a US report, the quality of tung oil produced in the country is better than that of our country after chemical analysis. Therefore, our country's exports were severely hit in foreign trade. If the authorities can actively improve the export commodities and standardize the standards, there may be hope of recovery in the future.

Recent Situation of Overseas Chinese: The recent situation of overseas Chinese in various parts of the United States is also affected by the failure to improve commodities. The commercial power of overseas Chinese in San Francisco has always been one of the best, but in recent years it has been in a slump. The Japanese are taking advantage of the situation to compete, and their products can cater to the tastes of Americans. Because it is difficult to compete, most of them have closed down, and the commercial power of the Japanese is growing day by day. They have also organized commodity exhibitions in the area, on the one hand using advertising to attract Americans to buy, and on the other hand guiding the improvement of commodities. Therefore, the status of overseas Chinese in various parts of the United States has been greatly damaged. The local impression of silk and electrical appliances produced in our country is still good in Singapore, because their prices are also lower than those in the local area. From this, it can be seen that if our country wants to restore its lost foreign commercial power, it must first start by improving the quality and standards of domestic goods, and the authorities should also have considerable restrictions so that its sales have a sound organization.

U.S. Commerce: The reason why U.S. commerce can develop so well is mostly due to the measures taken by the government authorities. Its organizations for assisting commerce include the domestic and foreign trade bureaus, with 25 branches domestically and 35 branches abroad, cooperative organizations, and the Bureau of Commerce, which control commercial power and establish import and export banks to provide loans and insurance, and export loan insurance. It promotes and supports commerce, exchanges commercial treaties, and on the one hand tries to limit the quantity of imported goods, and on the other hand encourages the export of commodities to dump them on foreign markets. Therefore, the industry and commerce in the United States are flourishing. I hope that our government should also adopt its strengths and gradually progress.
