Three Tea Merchants Sharing a Room: Over a Thousand Dollars Vanish 111

Wang Wenhuan's Wallet Found Empty; Fang Douwen Arrested in Nanjing and Sent Back to Shanghai for Theft 112

Fang Douwen, Wang Wenhuan, and Wang Xingwu, all from Anhui and engaged in the tea business, shared a residence at No. 4 Yuan Fengrun Tea Shop in Yi Ru Lane, 646 Tiantong Road. Between the 14th and 15th of this month, Wang Wenhuan noticed that 1,800 yuan in legal tender had mysteriously disappeared. Fang Douwen, who lived with him, also left that evening. Wang suspected Fang of theft and reported it to the Detective Department of the police station, requesting an investigation.

It was not until the day before yesterday that they learned Fang was in Nanjing. Consequently, Chinese Detective Zhao Qingkui requested official documents from the First Special Court and rushed to the capital to arrest Fang Douwen. He was brought back to Shanghai and detained at the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Fifth Criminal Tribunal of the First Special Court. The police station's lawyer, Mr. Qian Jiu, filed a public prosecution for theft under Article 320 of the Criminal Code, outlining the case. He stated that the victim, Wang Wenhuan, and the defendant, Fang Douwen, along with Wang Xingwu, were all tea merchants living in the same room. Wang Wenhuan's tea had been sold, and the money was deposited in the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank. Wang had recently withdrawn 2,000 yuan from the bank. After exchanging 200 yuan for five-yuan banknotes of the Bank of China, he placed the remaining 1,800 legal tender notes in his wallet without sealing it.

On the afternoon of the 14th of this month, at one o'clock, the plaintiff went out shopping and returned at eight o'clock. Wang Xingwu also went to the China Hotel to visit friends at six o'clock in the afternoon. Unexpectedly, the next day (the 15th), the plaintiff opened his wallet and discovered that 1,800 yuan in banknotes had disappeared. Furthermore, the defendant had left a note stating that he received an urgent phone call from Nanjing at nine o'clock on the 14th and had to leave immediately, without taking his luggage, saying he would return to Shanghai in two or three days. The plaintiff then reported it to the police station, but because he did not know the defendant's whereabouts in Nanjing, he could not be arrested. It was not until the 20th of this month that another tea merchant residing in the Yuan Fengrun Tea Shop, He Shengyuan, received a letter from the defendant, entrusting him to take care of his luggage, revealing that the defendant was staying at Chen Gongguan at No. 2 Mogan Road in Nanjing. The plaintiff informed the police station, and detectives went to the capital, transferred him to Shanghai.

At the police station, the defendant admitted to stealing the banknotes. Thirty-five yuan in legal tender was found on his person. He stated that he had spent 600 yuan, deposited 900 yuan in the Nanyang Shop on Sixiang Street in Nanjing, and 200 yuan with Xu Jili on Hongwu Road in Nanjing. Therefore, the case requested a postponement to recover the money.

The defendant, Fang Douwen, denied the theft, claiming that on that evening, a former legislator surnamed [omitted] called Yang Qi, who lived on [omitted] Road, instructing him to go to Nanjing overnight. Therefore, he rushed to Nanjing.

The presiding judge reviewed the statements and ordered the defendant to be detained pending a retrial in seven days.

Three Englishmen Accuse Gu Yubo of Fraud 113

Jointly Opened Meihua Bank, Found Malfeasance After Collapse 114

Three Englishmen – Yale, manager of Jardine, Matheson & Co. at 17 Jiangxi Road, Munroe, accountant at Yi Mow Lee, and Maleto – recently hired lawyers to file a complaint with the Criminal Court of the First Special Court in their capacity as directors of the Meihua Bank at 230 Jiujiang Road, which had been open for less than two months. They accused Gu Yubo, the Chinese general manager of the bank, of fraud and breach of trust. Yesterday morning, Judge Huang Risheng summoned them for questioning. The plaintiffs all appeared in court, but the defendant, Gu Yubo, did not appear because the address in the plaintiff's complaint, Gu's friend's home at 374 Haifang Road, was used for service of the summons, which he refused to accept.

During the hearing, the plaintiff Yale testified that the defendant, Gu Yubo, had initially prepared to establish the Daxin Industrial Bank, but due to shareholder issues, it did not open. Subsequently, he partnered with the plaintiffs to open the Meihua Bank, which was registered as Meihua Bank Limited with the British government in Hong Kong. It opened on April 8th of this year but collapsed on April 27th. Gu then went into hiding. After accountants Yi Mow Lee and audit staff member McKessack audited the accounts, they discovered that the defendant had used a fictitious name, Shanji, to overdraft 11,000 yuan from Meihua Bank. He also forged the official stamp of Meihua Bank and issued promissory notes, which he discounted with creditors such as the Xinkang Money Exchange, totaling over 20,000 yuan.

However, it is not yet clear whether there were other embezzlement or misappropriation. There is also concern that there may be other accomplices involved, and further accusations may be added. The defendant's current residence is uncertain, and a warrant for his arrest is requested for a thorough investigation.

Judge Huang reviewed the testimony and adjourned the hearing to the 31st, ordering the defendant to be summoned to court for questioning.

Number of Public Rickshaws Temporarily Unchanged 124

Regarding the question of whether the number of public rickshaws can be reduced, the relevant departments of the Shanghai Municipal Council have recently had detailed discussions. Qīngliáng Temple 125

The Story of Land Donation and House Construction 126

Renewed Hearing on Objection to Execution Yesterday 127

The case between Qinghai, the abbot of Qingliang Temple on Xinzha Road, and the Tonghe Foreign Firm's objection to execution was renewed yesterday morning at 8 AM by Judge Wang Qufei of the First Special Court in the Tenth Civil Tribunal. Onlookers included about thirty people, such as Chinese and Western gentlemen from the temple's maintenance committee and representatives from various organizations.

First, the plaintiff's agent, lawyer Lu Qi, stated that the second defendant, Sheng Yuyou, was in England and therefore could not sign an authorization. Therefore, his agent lawyer was not legally authorized to act on his behalf. However, the situation in this case is complicated, and in order to fully understand the case, it is necessary to explain in detail the previous lawsuits between Tonghe Foreign Firm and Qingliang Temple, the lease signed by both parties, and whether Tonghe Foreign Firm truly received the mortgage and has the right to sue.

The use of the disputed land in the Xin family garden by Xiaoliang Temple and the old houses on it dates back to around 1921. Initially, it was actually donated to the temple by Sheng Zhuangshi, Sheng Yuyou's grandmother. Therefore, after the Qi-Lu War in 1924, the plaintiff began fundraising to build new houses, such as temples and monastic halls, totaling more than one hundred rooms. By 1927, when the National Government investigated and confiscated Sheng's property, Sheng Zhuangshi, on the one hand, wanted to avoid government confiscation and, on the other hand, to prevent the temple from being unable to complete the construction within the five-year deadline after receiving the donation. Therefore, Zhuangshi unilaterally wrote a lease contract, instructing the plaintiff to stamp it as a win-win solution. Unexpectedly, Zhuangshi died shortly after exchanging contracts.

Initially, the Sheng family raised no objections. However, last year, Tonghe Foreign Firm, in the name of a mortgagee, came forward to sue for relocation and delivery of the house. In the original trial, it was not that the court did not notice that Tonghe Foreign Firm was not qualified as a plaintiff and had no right to sue. However, Sheng Yuyou testified that everything had already been transferred to Tonghe, so the original trial accepted the case. Moreover, it was found that the subject of the lawsuit was claimed to be over 350,000 yuan, while the original trial was decided in the summary court. Furthermore, in the first three hearings, the two defendants never presented the original

mortgage contract

to the court. The English version and translation on file are different in many places, and even the surnames of the mortgagor and guarantor are missing. Furthermore, the translation of the mortgage contract of the two defendants includes all the temples built and unfinished by the plaintiff on the disputed land as collateral. Even if it is mortgaged, it is not only in violation of the law but also absurd. How can the landowner have the right to mortgage the temples built by the temple, and even the unfinished houses can be mortgaged?

This is truly a strange story.

The plaintiff filed this lawsuit for objection to execution because their ownership was taken away.

At this point, Zuo Detao, the agent of Sheng Yuyou, stated that the plaintiff's lawsuit for objection to execution against Tonghe should require the plaintiff to respond to what request they have of Sheng Yuyou. This is a preliminary question. The court immediately asked lawyer Lu what

requests are there of Sheng?

Lawyer Lu replied that the plaintiff has no relationship with Tonghe. Because Tonghe, after receiving the mortgage, overstepped their authority and filed a lawsuit, causing the plaintiff to suffer damages due to the execution error. However, who the disputed house belongs to is Sheng's business. If Sheng does not object to the plaintiff's request, then the lawsuit against Sheng can be withdrawn. If Sheng does not agree with the plaintiff's claim, the plaintiff will naturally sue them together. The court stated that there are still procedural issues in this case and that the summons will be issued after a ruling.

Husband Brutal 128

Wife Dies Suddenly 129

Judge Orders Autopsy Due to Unclear Cause of Death 130

Peng Shou Zeng, a native of Gaoyou and owner of a broker shop at 738 Huade Road, is known for his violent temper. Four years ago, he married a woman surnamed Zhou from his hometown, who was now 26 years old. The morning before last, the couple had a dispute over household matters, and Peng allegedly beat his wife, causing her injuries. She fell to the ground and cried out in pain. Peng escorted her to Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment. However, that evening, Peng brought her home. At 11:45 PM, she suddenly died. Subsequently, the Yulin Road police station received a report and sent detectives to investigate. They transported the body to the Fei Lun Road morgue and took Peng into custody at the police station.

Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Tribunal of the First Special District Court. Municipal Council lawyer Zhang Shizhu requested detention for further investigation. Judge Su granted the request. At around 10 AM, Prosecutor Zhang was dispatched by the Prosecutor's Office to the morgue to inspect the body. Immediately after examining the body, he ascended to the public case. Zhou Caiyuan, the deceased's brother, claimed that he worked at a school on Qiqihar Road. After his sister was injured, he was notified and went to see her. His sister told him that her little stomach had been kicked by her husband with a leather shoe, but it was unintentional, so she asked for leniency. Mao Yushi, a woman from Yangzhou, testified that she lived in the stove room of the defendant's house and returned late after leaving early. She said that the couple often fought and played. That morning, she only saw Peng slightly hit his wife on the back, but she did not see anything else.

When questioned, the defendant denied kicking. In order to clarify the truth of the deceased's death, Mr. Zhang ordered an autopsy on the already deceased Peng Zhoushi. As the cause of death is currently unknown, it will be handed over to a forensic doctor for autopsy and further verification. After the autopsy, the body will be handed over to the deceased's brother, Zhou Caiyuan, for burial.

Tram Fares 133

To Be Changed to New Currency 134

Approved by the Municipal Council 135

Since the National Government issued the decimal new currency, the Shanghai Tram Company has been calculating copper coins at three per fen, which is extremely convenient. Recently, the company submitted a request to the Municipal Council to revise the fare table, calculating everything using the new currency system. This matter was discussed by the Municipal Council's Public Utilities Committee a few days ago. It was the general opinion that the purpose of this change in fares was to promote the new currency and facilitate passengers, and that there was no intention to increase fares. The calculation method is based on the recent half-fen standard, and the Public Bus Company had already been granted the same request in mid-March of this year. Therefore, it seems appropriate to approve the Tram Company's request. It has now been submitted to the board of directors for approval and is expected to be implemented soon.

Municipal Council Hiring 136

Pathologist 137

People of All Nationalities May Apply 138

The Municipal Council issued a notice yesterday, stating that the Municipal Council's Health Department is now seeking to employ one male Assistant Pathologist, regardless of nationality. However, the age must be at least 25 years old and no more than 30 years old, and they must be unmarried. The candidate must have qualifications in internal and surgical medicine that are registrable and meet university standards. Holding a public health certificate (or equivalent document) is preferred but not required. A candidate with tropical medicine experience is even more qualified. In any case, they must have experience in the daily work of a pathological laboratory and practical knowledge of manufacturing large quantities of bacterial injections, and must be able to speak fluent English and write smooth English. The salary will be paid according to the salary scale, which can be obtained from the Health Department. The terms of service are limited to those applicable to locally employed personnel. The proposed candidate must first undergo a rigorous physical examination to determine whether their physical condition is suitable. The appointed person must be assigned to any part of the Health Department for work. Applicants must fill out the application form in their own handwriting and submit it along with three recent certificates to the Director of the Health Department no later than August 17 of this year. The application form should be sealed and the words "Assistant Pathologist" should be written on the cover. Applicants must not solicit the help of the board members and (or) committee members to speak on their behalf, or ask them to write letters of recommendation or introduction, otherwise their qualifications will be cancelled. This special announcement is for general knowledge.

Umbrella Merchants Association 139

Improving the Quality of Chinese Umbrellas 140

Sales in Southeast Asia Decreasing Daily 141

Overseas Chinese Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter Requesting Improvement 142

Paper umbrellas made in our country are sold in large quantities in the Southeast Asian islands. However, in recent years, sales have been decreasing daily. According to investigations, on the one hand, it is because Western umbrellas produced in Japan are being promoted more widely in that area, encroaching on the market for Chinese umbrellas. On the other hand, it is because the quality of Chinese umbrellas has been deteriorating, and merchants are unwilling to sell them. The oil used in Chinese umbrellas was originally tung oil, but in recent years, the price of tung oil has been high, causing umbrella merchants to switch to mixed oils, which causes the umbrella paper to tear and break. The Overseas Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Southeast Asia sent a letter to Chinese umbrella merchants, asking them to improve the situation. It is now known that the Umbrella Merchants Association has sent personnel to Zhejiang and Guangdong to investigate and provide guidance at any time, in order to ensure the purity of the quality of paper umbrellas, thereby reversing the decline in sales in Southeast Asia.

Social Affairs Bureau Cracking Down on 143

Medical Practice Under False Pretenses 144

Pan Qinzhai is a Personal Organization 145

Claiming to Provide Medical Treatment but Actually Collecting Money 146

The Social Affairs Bureau of this city yesterday sent letters to the Municipal Party Committee, the Public Security Bureau, and other agencies, stating that they had received Letter No. 8529 from the Health Bureau, which stated that Pan Qinzhai, a Chinese medicine practitioner from Tongji Shantang at 74 Tangjiawan Road, had submitted a request to register a clinic for providing medical treatment. The bureau had sent personnel to investigate and found that the clinic's equipment was extremely simple. However, since Shantang is a public charitable organization, the bureau did not know whether it had been approved by your bureau for registration and requested a reply for handling. After sending personnel to investigate, it was reported that Pan Qinzhai, a Chinese medicine practitioner from Taizhou, stated that the hall was opened in April of this year, and he was solely responsible, with no organization or charter. Those who seek treatment pay a fee of two jiao, but medicine is free. However, the hall's equipment is extremely simple, with only three or four small bottles of medicine. The words "Tongji Shantang" are prominently displayed in the middle of the road, which is very conspicuous. Therefore, there is a suspicion that the hall is a personal clinic using the name of a charitable organization to attract customers, which should be cracked down on. In addition to ordering the organization to be disbanded and all signboards removed, you are requested to investigate and take action.

Kidnapped Victim and Searched Him on Board 152

Jiang Xisheng Only Had a Savings Account Book 153

Gang Extremely Disappointed and Released Jiang 154

Wang Xinggao 155

Found Guarantor for 20,000 Yuan 156

Regained Freedom the Day Before Yesterday 157

Wang Xinggao, a native of Funing who used to work in the military and police and is suspected of abetting the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, appealed to the High Court Branch after being sentenced to life imprisonment by the Second Special Court in the first instance. After repeated court investigations and trials, the court found no substantial evidence of a crime. On the 26th of last month, the court overturned the original judgment and declared him innocent. Later, Wang applied to suspend detention during the appeal period and was ordered to provide a 10,000-yuan guarantor to ensure his appearance when summoned. His family found six stores to jointly guarantee Wang's release. Subsequently, because the Police Affairs Office did not accept the High Court Branch's judgment on appeal and requested the prosecutor of the High Court Branch to appeal to the Supreme Court, the Criminal Tribunal of the High Court Branch, considering that the case was already in the appeal process due to the Police Affairs Office's appeal, considered Wang Xinggao's bail amount insufficient. Therefore, the court summoned Wang a few days ago and instructed him to increase the guarantee amount by 10,000 yuan, requiring a 20,000-yuan written guarantee. During the period for finding a guarantor, he was temporarily detained. Eventually, Wang's family managed to find a guarantor through various channels, and the guarantee procedures were completed on the day before yesterday. Wang Xinggao was then released for the second time and regained his freedom.

Cao Jingui Tried for Stabbing Two People in Gambling Dispute 169

Cao Jingui, a 20-year-old from Nanhui, Pudong, a shop assistant at the Ren Da Leather Goods Store at 178 Broadway, had an argument and fight with his colleague Xue Jinbo over a gambling dispute around 9:00 pm on the 12th of this month. He stabbed Xue in the abdomen with a knife, causing his intestines to spill out. Xue fell to the ground and cried for help. Seeing the serious consequences, Cao fled towards the Oriental Wharf on Broadway. Yu Wenbing, a native of Nantong and a shop assistant at the neighboring Ren Chang Leather Goods Store, helped to chase him. Yu was also stabbed in the left arm, hand, chest, and wrist. As a result, colleagues Pu Changsheng and the Japanese police officer from No. 117, along with Chinese detective Zhang Desheng, captured Cao. The murder weapon, a knife, was thrown into the Huangpu River. The injured Xue and Yu were taken to the Jen Ji Hospital for treatment. The suspect Cao was sent to the First Special District Court, where he testified that Pu Changsheng was the actual assailant. The judge ordered him to be detained for further investigation. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhong Qing continued the trial in the Third Criminal Court. Mr. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Shanghai Municipal Council, stated that the injured Xue Jinbo had not recovered and could not appear in court to testify. However, Yu Wenbing and Pu Changsheng were present and requested to be questioned. Pu Changsheng claimed that he saw the defendant running away from the wharf, chased by Ma Anxiang, who was shouting for help. He stopped Cao and handed him over to the Japanese police officer from No. 117. He did not know why. The defendant's claim that he used a knife to stab the two victims was a false accusation. Yu Wenbing, whose injuries had slightly healed, testified that he knew the defendant. The defendant's resentment towards Xue Jinbo was not about mahjong, but because Xue had an affair with the defendant's sister, which he felt was a great loss of face, leading to his actions. He saw Cao stab Xue in the abdomen and flee towards the wharf. He stopped him, and Cao stabbed him several times in the hand and shoulder with a leather-cutting knife before escaping. His left wrist tendon was severed, and he feared that his hand would be disabled. The defendant insisted that the incident started with a mahjong game, with seven people on Xue Jinbo's side. Pu Changsheng dragged him out to beat him, and Pu accidentally stabbed Xue and Yu while trying to stab him with a knife. The testimony was inconsistent, and Judge Zhong Qing ordered him to be detained and re-examined after Xue recovered from his injuries.

Obstetrics Expert

Dr. Qu Shaoheng Saves a Pregnant Woman's Life: Fetus Upside Down in Womb, Family Weeping; Dr. Qu Performs Surgery, Sweating Profusely 173

Cao Ding, the 38-year-old wife of Cao Guanyuan of Qingning Temple, Pudong, had given birth to nine children. Last November, her menstrual cycle suddenly stopped, and she became pregnant again. Starting on the 10th of this month, she had been bleeding continuously every day. In the past three days, the bleeding had increased, causing her to faint several times and lose color in her face. Although traditional midwives had repeatedly performed procedures, they were ineffective. On the morning of the 24th, Dr. Qu Duizhen, an obstetrics expert from Xinlu, Pudong, was invited for examination. After examination, Dr. Qu said it was a difficult labor, and immediately sent a telegram inviting her uncle, Dr. Qu Boheng (院长 of the Sheng Sheng Hospital on Route Saussier in the French Concession of Shanghai), to perform the procedure. Around 11:00 am, Dr. Qu led Zhu Shijing, Yao Weixin, Yu Heiying, Wu Biyi, Xu Xinbao, Jin Yajun, and other assistants to the Cao residence. At that time, the delivery room was packed with people, all weeping and crying. Dr. Qu remained calm and sterilized the area. After examination, he determined that it was the same as what Dr. Duizhen had said. He immediately began the operation. Dr. Qu inserted his hand deep into the uterus, almost up to his elbow. Soon after, he reversed the position of the fetus, changing its face position to a foot position. In a few minutes, the fetus and placenta were completely expelled. The crisis was over. Dr. Qu was extremely exhausted and sweating profusely. Onlookers praised him as a living Buddha. After the procedure, Dr. Qu told the crowd that it was a pity that they had adhered to old practices and delayed for so many days, causing the fetus to die in vain. If they had sought the help of a scientific midwife earlier, the child's life could have been saved. He sighed deeply.

National Products Movement Federation: Activities of Various Groups 174

The Yangtze River Inspection Group, the Women's Use of National Products Group, and the Student Summer Vacation Promotion of National Products Group of the Shanghai National Products Movement Federation have been actively preparing and have been established one after another. Details are as follows:

Yangtze River Inspection Group: In order to promote the use of national products by people in various regions, the federation's committee meeting decided to establish a Yangtze River Inspection Group and invited Lin Kecong, Huang Shuipei, and Lu Lihua to be members. Unable to spare the time, they declined. The group is now looking for suitable talent. Once decided, they will depart for Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Anhui, Hubei, Shandong, and other regions to conduct inspections. Women's Use Group: The federation believes that women are housewives and their words and deeds are enough to influence men. The sharp decline in imports over the years has proven that women's promotion can achieve twice the result with half the effort. Therefore, they initiated the Women's Use of National Products Group and invited female compatriots several times to discuss methods, which were all supported by the female community. The federation decided to establish the Women's Use Group at the same time as the Yangtze River Inspection Group departs.

Summer Vacation Promotion Group: Last month, the group invited principals and teachers from large and small schools in the city and decided to take advantage of the summer vacation period to have students promote the use of national products in all directions. At that time, the persons in charge of the schools believed that using national products was the duty of the people, and that students promoting them during the holidays would cultivate their ability to serve society. Therefore, they all expressed sympathy. According to a report from the Xin Sheng News Agency, more than 30 schools, including Nanli and Huadong, have been formally established.

The China Child Welfare Association has decided to establish a housemaid training institute to help housemaids in Shanghai. Wang Fengzhen vs. Shen Jinzhi: New Evidence on Age May Exist; Defendant Ordered to Appear in Court in 8,000 Yuan Compensation Case 179

Shen Jinzhi, also known as Shen Keren, the young owner of the Shen Wanxing Wick and Cattail Mat Store at No. 30-32, Yongyou Lane, Damatou Inside Ma Road, South City, relied on his family wealth and his fair complexion to indulge in pleasure in brothels. He became intimate with Wang Fengzhen, a prostitute from the Yunlou brothel between Guangxi Road and Shantou Road. They extinguished the candles and made a pact to stay together, and took a photo together at Tiger Hill. The two had already agreed to be husband and wife, but his family strongly opposed it and had already arranged a marriage for him with Xia Hefang, a wealthy woman. Therefore, Shen and Fengzhen had once signed an agreement to separate. In the winter of last year, the two rekindled their love. The two then voluntarily entered into a contract, stating that if the man abandoned the woman, he would have to compensate her 8,000 yuan; if the woman abandoned the man, she would have to compensate him 5,000 yuan. However, on April 19 of this year, Shen Jinzhi finally followed his parents' wishes and married Xia Hefang at the Lake Club. From then on, the lovers went their separate ways. Wang Fengzhen then took the agreement to the local court to request a judgment ordering him to fulfill the 8,000 yuan compensation as agreed. Both parties were listed as 22 years old on the complaint. Shen Jinzhi argued that he was only 21 years old and had not yet had his birthday when the agreement was signed. He was under 20 years old and did not have the capacity to act under the law and was not liable for the contract. The dispute over age has continued until now and has not been resolved. The court ordered both parties to provide evidence in their favor. At yesterday's hearing, the defendant did not appear. The plaintiff, accompanied by her lawyer, stated that the plaintiff had now discovered new evidence that could prove that the defendant was 22 years old this year, but needed a 10-day extension to present it. The official immediately approved and ordered the defendant's lawyer to order the defendant to appear in court in person for questioning next time.

Letter 190

To the Editor: I recently read in the news column of the Shen Bao on the 21st of this month a report that lawyer Chen Zemin was accused of privately selling the property of his client to pay off public fees. It stated that Zhu Zhang deposited the deed with lawyer Chen Zemin, but unexpectedly, the field property was sold to the local headman Zuo Yaoqing twenty-four years ago. Now, the three sisters, Zhang Zhu Fuying, etc., claiming that they have three-fifths of the co-ownership of the field property, have filed a lawsuit with the local court against their mother Zhu Zhang, lawyer Chen Zemin, and local headman Zuo Yaoqing for privately selling other people's real estate. This is not in accordance with the facts. The sale of the above-mentioned property was directly made by Zhu Zhang to Zuo Yaoqing. Zhu Zhang and Yaoqing requested the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau to survey and map the land. There is an original case in the Land Bureau that can prove this. The original graves on the land were personally moved elsewhere by Zhu Zhang. Lawyer Chen had no knowledge of it. However, when Zuo Yaoqing made the payment, because he did not trust Zhu Zhang, he only entrusted lawyer Chen to issue a receipt on his behalf, as proof only. The various points reported by your newspaper are mostly untrue. Our lawyers are entrusted by lawyer Chen to handle the litigation of this case. We hereby send the details in a letter, hoping that you will make corrections to avoid confusion. Sincerely, Lawyers Zhao Futing and Wu Zhaozhen, July 24th.

Our World Games Delegation: Grand Arrival in Berlin; Received an Unexpectedly Warm Welcome; The Blue Sky with a White Sun Flag Raised at the Sports Field 191

National United Press, Berlin, July 23rd: Before the special train from Venice arrived, the station was already full of people welcoming the Chinese World Games athletes. The platform of the station was decorated with flowers and Chinese flags, making it extremely beautiful. All the overseas Chinese in Berlin, led by Ambassador Cheng Tianfang, arrived at the station to welcome them. The German government representative, Kirsha, the chairman of the World Games Organizing Committee, Rivat, etc., also arrived at the station to participate in the welcome.

When the special train arrived, military music played the Chinese national anthem. 140 athletes and instructors, and 29 students, filed out. At the station, the government representative, Kirsha, first exchanged greetings and welcomed them. Then, the leader of the delegation, Shen Siliang, briefly said a few words. The entire team then walked out of the station. Their attire was neat and their formation was dignified, attracting much attention. After exiting the station, they were sent to the City Hall for a welcome reception in specially prepared buses. They were warmly welcomed by the people along the way.

Mayor Robert, in his welcoming speech at the City Hall, said that although China has only sent representatives to participate in the World Games for the first time, Chinese sports history has thousands of years of background. Afterwards, the representatives took specially prepared cars to the Olympic Village. At the same time, the Blue Sky with a White Sun and Red Earth flag was raised high at the gate of the World Games venue. According to the order of arrival, China is twenty-fourth.

The Chinese athlete representatives expressed their delight at arriving in Berlin after traveling halfway around the world. The leader of the delegation, Shen Siliang, said that the grand and solemn welcome they received in Berlin was beyond their expectations. He also said that although the Chinese athletes may not win medals, they will benefit from witnessing the World Games, which will be helpful for the next World Games.

(National United Press, Berlin, 24) The most shocking news when the American World Games team arrived in Berlin was the announcement by the American World Games Committee that it had canceled the qualification of Mrs. Holm Charette, the 1932 Los Angeles World Games 100-meter backstroke champion. Education News

Overview of Scientific Research by Faculty Members of National Universities: 502 Research Projects Completed 207

In order to encourage and promote scientific research by faculty members of national universities, the Ministry of Education has issued a notice to all specialized schools and above nationwide since the 23rd academic year, hoping that faculty members of each school will pay attention to experimentation based on their teaching and research experience. If there are creations and inventions, rewards will be given accordingly. The Ministry of Education is now investigating the actual situation of scientific research by faculty members of all specialized schools nationwide. According to reports up to the 23rd academic year, national, provincial, private specialized schools, colleges, universities, and public specialized schools nationwide are conducting research by subject. Taking the study of a certain thing as a special topic, for example, a professor at Tsinghua University studying optics is inventing a telephoto lens that makes the image clear. If this optical research is taken as a special topic for near photography, according to this statistics, the number of research topics by faculty members of specialized schools and above nationwide is as follows: In terms of practical subjects, 91 topics in science, 41 in agriculture and forestry, 6 in engineering, and 236 in medicine (mostly at Peking Union Medical College Hospital) have been completed. 114 topics in science, 76 in agriculture and forestry, 17 in engineering, and 22 in medicine are still under research and have not been completed. In terms of the above-mentioned practical subjects, a total of 374 topics have been completed and 229 topics have not been completed. In terms of humanities subjects, 64 topics in literature and art (a professor studied dialects in various parts of the country and has a special work on this, and obtained a doctorate degree abroad), 29 in law and politics, 28 in education, and 7 in commerce have been completed. 98 topics in literature and art, 41 in law and politics, 28 in education, and 9 in commerce are still under research and have not been completed. In terms of the above-mentioned humanities subjects, a total of 128 topics have been completed and 176 topics have not been completed. In total, 502 topics have been completed and 405 topics are still under research. Although the Ministry of Education promoted and rewarded research by faculty members of universities in the 20th academic year, some professors at various schools had already started studying certain sciences in 1915, but the research has not yet been successful. Therefore, many of the 405 topics that are still under research in the 23rd year survey report are similar to this. In the future, the Ministry of Education plans to compile an index of the detailed topics researched by each school as a reference for the national academic community. The success of this type of research topic is of great value to the academic community.

Regulations on Private Chinese Schools in the Public Concession Requesting Subsidies: Petitions Must Be Submitted to the Bureau Before September 15th 208

In order to promote education within the concession, the Public Concession Bureau allocates a fixed amount of money each year as subsidies for Chinese and Western schools within the concession. All private Chinese schools within the concession whose management, equipment, and teaching performance are deemed satisfactory by the Bureau and who are indeed in need of economic subsidies may apply to the Bureau for the grant of this subsidy. The method of application is as follows: All schools registered with the Municipal Education Bureau should first submit a request to the Municipal Education Bureau, which will issue the forms and regulations prepared by the Bureau. Then, the principals of each school should fill out and stamp them, and the Municipal Education Bureau will review and approve them before submitting them to the Bureau for review and decision. Those who have not been registered with the Municipal Education Bureau may directly request the Bureau's Education Department to issue the forms for the year, fill them out in accordance with the regulations, and submit them to the Department for review and processing. In addition, Western children's schools in the concession and special donation areas may also apply to the Bureau's Education Department for subsidies. The procedure is the same as for Chinese schools that have not been registered with the Municipal Education Bureau. However, those who wish to receive the subsidies for the 1937 academic year must submit these forms and petitions no later than September 15th of this year.

Ministry of Education Broadcast: Temporarily Suspended Today; Secondary Schools Have a Holiday 213

Broadcasting Education Committee Rules Promulgated by the Ministry of Education 214

On the 23rd, the Ministry of Education issued an order to abolish the previous ten articles of the Broadcasting Education Design Committee rules and promulgated nine articles of the Ministry of Education Broadcasting Education Committee rules. The original text is as follows: Article 1: The Ministry of Education establishes the Broadcasting Education Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee") to improve the efficiency of broadcasting education. Article 2: The Committee consists of seven to nine members, who are appointed or assigned by the Minister of Education from the following personnel: (1) Representative of the Central Broadcasting Administration; (2) Three to five broadcasting education technology or education experts; (3) Directors of the General Education Department, the General Affairs Department, and the Social Education Department of the Ministry of Education. Article 3: The Committee shall have one chairman who handles daily affairs. The Director of the Social Education Department of the Ministry of Education shall serve as the chairman. The Committee may have one secretary, who shall be appointed by the Minister of Education from specialized personnel. Article 4: The duties of the Committee are as follows: (1) Planning methods for broadcasting programs and supplying broadcasting materials; (2) Planning the promotion of broadcasting education undertakings; (3) Providing technical guidance; (4) Studying all issues related to broadcasting education. Article 5: Resolutions of the Committee shall be submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation. Article 6: The affairs of the Committee shall be handled concurrently by the staff of the relevant departments of the Ministry of Education. Article 7: The Committee shall hold a regular meeting once a month, convened by the chairman. Article 8: Committee members shall be unpaid, but out-of-town committee members may be reimbursed for travel expenses when attending meetings in Beijing. Article 9: These rules shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Forestry Industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Write to Zhejiang University, Requesting Preservation of the Forestry Department 215

(Zhenjiang News) Zeng Jikuan, Deputy Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Agricultural Improvement Management Committee, and Chen Zhi, a technician, along with Li Yingong, Zhang Fuyan, Yao Chuanfa, Pi Zuoqiong, An Han, Yu Kuang, Ling Daoyang, Tu Rong, Zhu Huifang, Liang Xi, Shao Jun, and other leading figures in the forestry industry in Beijing, recently heard that after Dean Wu Fuzhen of the College of Agriculture of Zhejiang University took office, he immediately abolished the Forestry Department. However, the forestry department of the university has been operating for twenty-four years. How can such a long-standing institution be abolished rashly based on the proposals of one or two people from the university or college? If this happens, forestry institutions will be in constant jeopardy. Therefore, Zeng and others were extremely shocked upon hearing the news. In addition to submitting a request to President Jiang and the Ministry of Education, led by the Chinese Forestry Society, requesting that the university authorities handle the matter with caution, they also sent a friendly letter to Dean Wu, hoping that he would consider the matter in order to salvage the situation.

Sichuan University in the Past Year (II) 218

(6) Significant Increase in Books and Equipment

Since the last term, the university has paid exceptional attention to book equipment. This year's book budget is 80,000 yuan, and the expansion of the equipment of the College of Science is also 80,000 yuan. Large quantities of books arrive at the library every week. A considerable number of books that have been ordered are still en route.

(7) Emphasis on Physical Education

Because the students of Sichuan Province are known to be physically weak, the university pays special attention to physical education. A physical education guidance committee and a physical education department are established to be responsible for designing and promoting physical education throughout the university. This year, the university held various sports competitions twice, a spring sports meet once, and organized representative teams to participate in competitions outside the university, with good results. In terms of equipment, in addition to the construction of two 400-meter running tracks, two straight tracks of more than 200 meters, two soccer fields, eight basketball courts, twelve tennis courts, and five volleyball courts, all kinds of sports equipment are available. It is said that Mr. Huang Zhongfu, who was famous for sports in Tsinghua University and is now studying physical education in the United States, has been hired to serve as the director of physical education next year, and the facilities for physical education will definitely make greater progress.

(8) Organization of the Southwest Social Science Research Center

Because Sichuan is located in the western frontier and the social situation has many unique aspects that need to be investigated in order to discover facts and provide reference for social scientists, the university specially organized the Southwest Social Science Research Center this term. It conducts thorough investigations and research on economic and folk customs issues in Sichuan Province and the southwestern border. The center has an advisory committee. In addition to the deans and secretary-general of the university's colleges as ex-officio members, it also hires Chen Tongfu, an internationally renowned labor issue expert and current professor at National Tsinghua University, Zhou Gengsheng, an international law expert and current professor at Wuhan University, Hu Xiansu, a biologist expert and current director of the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society of China, and Tao Menghe, a sociologist expert and director of the Social Research Institute of the Academia Sinica, as committee members. He Lian, a famous economist and dean of the School of Business and director of the Economic Research Institute of Nankai University, serves as the chairman of the advisory committee. Bao Juemin, Ye Qianji, Zhang Xiyang, and Gu Yuantian, members of the Sichuan Economic Survey Team of Nankai University, are researchers and are actively carrying out investigations. They went to Guanxian and Pixian counties last month for investigation and are said to be going to Pengxian and Tangqing counties soon.

(9) Establishment of the Public Legal Advisory Office

Because the College of Law lacks practical experimental materials, there are shortcomings in understanding social governance methods. This term, the College of Law specially established a Public Legal Advisory Office to answer the public's legal questions, so that students can have practical experience, and legal knowledge can also be popularized to the general public. Since its establishment, it has been highly praised by people from all walks of life, and letters requesting guidance or advice have been received in an endless stream. This is one aspect of the university's service to society.

(10) Extracurricular Activities

The university strongly promotes extracurricular activities for students. For example, the research societies of various departments of the university have been established this year, and each has achieved considerable results. The university also hires several music instructors and one drama instructor to guide students in researching music and drama. Therefore, the university's Music Research Society and Drama Research Society have performed several times this year and have won high praise from people from all walks of life.

In general, the university is located in Chengdu, which is rich in products, and the cost of living is lower than that of the Yangtze River and coastal areas. Each student can spend 110 to 120 yuan per term. If they are a little frugal, they can spend 100 yuan per term. If the university can continue to develop and keep pace with other universities in the country, it will undoubtedly be a paradise for students in the southwest to study.

(The End)

The school is run in the most complete manner, with high standards and a high reputation in society. The teachers are commercial experts and social celebrities. There are also two specialized practice rooms, one specializing in commercial common sense, display and arrangement of goods, etc., and the other estimating the prices of goods. In these two laboratories, teachers specialize in teaching students the methods of evaluating the value of goods, sales methods, methods of receiving buyers, and window cabinet layout and display, all of which are the most practical subjects. The Polish government also encourages and promotes it, so that the effect of vocational education can be achieved.

Yesterday, when American cotton opened, each month rose or fell by one pound note. Investigation: Shanghai Tea Exports Surge in June 233

According to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Report from the Ministry of Industry, Shanghai's tea exports in June amounted to 39,607.13 metric tons of green tea, 12,908.77 metric tons of black tea, and 1,880.47 metric tons of other teas, totaling 54,396.37 metric tons. Page 17

Shen Bao Women's Special

Woolen Fabrics Only Have Sporadic Transactions 234

Yesterday, the woolen fabric market was quiet and sluggish, with only sporadic transactions. The number of brokers from nearby markets attending tea gatherings decreased. Prices remained similar to the day before. White plain broadcloth continued to be slow-moving. Tianxiang broadcloth sold for one yuan, three jiao, seven fen, and a half. Lihe white plain woolen fabric was at five yuan, three jiao, Yide at five yuan, one jiao, Yiji at three yuan, eight jiao, and Fengyu Baishuifang white serge sold for five yuan, seven jiao, and a half. Yiji Daoxiancao was at four yuan, seven jiao, and a half. Japanese-made Sima Xiangru was at three yuan, seven jiao, and the second-grade Jiangbian at three yuan, three jiao. Paris floral and plain fabrics, however, showed a continued positive trend.

Grains: Price Limits Restrict, Futures Powder Market Becomes Stagnant, Imported Wheat Prices Rise Frequently 235

Yesterday, the flour market, after opening in the morning, showed generally stable prices across various months. Imported wheat quotations showed Chicago up one, two, or three jiao, and Canada up four or five jiao. Market sentiment, constrained by price limits on the current month, resulted in a stagnant situation. Current total quantities were reportedly not large, but positions could not be left uncovered, so the price reached the limit, unable to fall further. For forward months, there was slight business from merchant guilds, and sentiment was quite positive, with August and September up one fen compared to the previous day, and other months up one and a half fen. By the afternoon opening, the current month remained unchanged, while forward months saw some profit-taking due to client cessation, falling back nearly a fen compared to the morning. However, compared to the previous day's close, they were still up two and a half to seven and a half li.

Imported Wheat Continues to Rise, Wheat Futures Market Appears Quite Firm, Market Prices Gradually Approach Imported Wheat Prices 236

Yesterday, the wheat futures market, after opening in the morning, saw prices trending steadily upward for all months. Imported wheat quotations rose again by one, two, three, four, or five jiao. Sentiment among industry insiders and outsiders inevitably anticipated further gains. As the settlement date for the current month approached, merchants mostly withdrew their holdings and rolled them into forward months, causing tightness in the current month, rising as high as six jiao. Forward month transactions were also clear, only at two or three fen. By the afternoon opening, the current month trended slightly flat, falling back by two fen, but forward months saw a bullish atmosphere and gradual price increases due to large outside firms taking positions. September and October rose six or seven fen compared to the previous day, while others rose two, three, or four fen. Given the current situation, if prices rise further, they will approach parity with imported wheat, which would be a dangerous situation. The spot wheat market remained stable, similar to yesterday, with Kaiming Guangshahe wheat at four yuan, five jiao, seven fen, Bengbu wheat at four yuan, five jiao, six fen, Suqian wheat at four yuan, five jiao, three fen, Huaian wheat at four yuan, five jiao, Daqiao wheat at four yuan, four jiao, seven fen, Jiangbei wheat at four yuan, four jiao, and a half, Anqing wheat at four yuan, three jiao, nine fen, second grade two jiao, six fen, Hankou wheat at four yuan, three jiao, seven fen, Shaobo wheat at four yuan, three jiao, two or three fen, and Wuhu wheat at four yuan, two jiao, two fen, with Fuxin handling 4,000 bags and Shenda handling 2,000 bags.

Early Rice Soon to Arrive, Old Rice Anxiously Seeking Sale 237

Yesterday, the Ke Hsien market condition was that because early rice from various places will soon be on the market, and reports state that Wuhu has already been harvested, with prices only around six yuan, five jiao, ample rice reserves in various places are depreciating in price and seeking sales. In Shanghai, stockpiles of Du Geng, imported Ke Hsien are particularly large. It is said that there are still 200,000 bags of He Xia Geng rice accumulated from last year, so sentiment is even softer. Merchants and hoarders are all trying to sell at any price. Although sales by various local merchant guilds are still good, market prices have fallen by nearly one jiao to one jiao and a half. The total daily output of 5,000 bags of Jiangxi, Hunan, and Taizhou rice was divided among Ningbo, Shantou, local streets, and inland areas.

White Geng and Du Jian Fall Further by One Jiao 238

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the total supply from various merchant guilds was over twenty companies, with a total of more than 4,000 shi of goods, mostly thick early Geng rice. However, sales on the local street market remained weak. The Dalian and Weihai guilds only handled a thin amount of thin rice, about 200 bags. Therefore, the market situation was even more sluggish. The market prices for thick early Geng rice and thin rice all fell by one jiao or more. Du Yang Jian rice also depreciated by a few fen. The Yin Bian Yuan brand was still able to maintain its price. (North Shanghai) Yesterday, there were seventeen or eighteen ships from He Xia and other places. The market removed goods from various guilds. High-quality white Geng rice was stagnant, while medium and lower grades saw slight sales. High-priced goods fell by one jiao, while medium and lower grades were sluggish by a few fen. Thin rice was scarce, and prices remained firm. Yang Jian rice was stagnant, with high-priced goods falling by five or six fen. Medium and lower grades were cut by more than one jiao. Du Bu Jian rice fell by nearly one jiao. Ke Hsien rice was short by more than one jiao. Yin Bian Yuan remained stable, and prices for all other goods were soft.

Soybean Cakes See Sudden Brisk Sales in Shantou 239

Recently, the soybean cake sales market saw a sudden surge in orders from the Shantou merchant guild. Yesterday, market prices rose by two fen in the morning and afternoon. Citywide transactions showed 1,100 pieces of various factory Four Brand cakes, with orders for 20,000 pieces to be delivered the day after tomorrow, 7,500 pieces for delivery at the end of the month, and 17,000 pieces for delivery in the first half of August. Other local factory black cakes saw transactions of 500 pieces, and Lun Shahe Guangbian cakes saw 2,000 pieces. The overall situation was still firm. New yellow soybeans continued to see a higher-for-lower grading situation. Oil factories continued to place orders, and various merchant guilds tirelessly removed goods, leading to good sentiment. Orders included over 1,000 bags of Chengmen beans, 300-400 bags of Sanyang beans, 20 bags of Jiangqiao beans, 100 bags of Hankou June white beans, and 300 bags of Shaoxing and Quzhou new beans. Factories purchased four carloads of Kaiyuan old beans. The local street Ningbo and other areas purchased 200 bags of Sipingjie large-grain beans and over 600 bags of Sha Huang and Du beans.

Finance: Pure Gold Falls, Standard Gold Becomes More Difficult to Rise: Although There Was a Slight Rebound Midway, It Was Very Brief 240

The gold market yesterday saw pure gold fall, and sentiment became even more exhausted. The decline continued. There was a slight rebound midway, but unfortunately, buying interest was only temporary. The result was another decline of two jiao. Initial morning indications showed that overseas silver markets in England and America were flat, and the forward price of Montrie silver was also unchanged. Exchange rates were lower. London raw gold fell by one and a half pence. Central Bank official rates showed England and America flat, and the Customs Gold Unit fell by two li. The standard gold price was announced, lowered to 1,128 yuan. Outside-market preliminary trading opened at 31 yuan to 1 yuan and a half. Xianghe, Tongyu, Run, Qian, and Changxiang sold off, falling to a price of one yuan. Large firms took advantage of the low price to maintain and stabilize the market. The morning opening was low, but large firms slightly covered positions after opening, gradually flattening out the market. HSBC official rates showed England and America flat, with slight fluctuations. After entering the market, short sellers entered.
