One-Sided View of Chastity 246

— Lin Wen

What is chastity? Chastity is the standard of human behavior. A woman who can meet this standard, without harming others but benefiting herself, is moral. But how can the establishment of morality be realized in an era of male dominance? In the past—and actually now as well—women were appendages of men. If a wife died, or even if she was not enough to satisfy her husband's desires, the husband could take concubines and frequent prostitutes again and again. If a woman's husband died and she could not satisfy her desires, she could only reluctantly suppress them, otherwise it would be difficult to gain public sympathy. This completely oppresses women from the standpoint of male power expansion. Our country has what is called the "seven grounds for divorce," which established the chastity of women and exclusively their bodies. This concept still exists today!

Now, although there are many people who advocate that chastity must be mutually maintained, what are the results it creates? On the surface, it seems to have shattered the illusion of male power expansion and excited people's modern thinking. But in reality, this anticipated hope, no matter how many times it is mentioned, cannot be universally realized! This is clear because the economic status and decline in productive capacity of women inevitably leads to this result.

In Chinese society, where female occupations are extremely difficult, the lives of women often depend on men. Therefore, women cannot help but cater to the needs of men and strive to maintain their chastity. Therefore, the dependence of women is the power that consolidates male power. We clearly know that the sanctions of male power undoubtedly deprive women of their autonomy!

No. 27 If women want to completely break this one-sided concept of chastity, they must exert their perseverance and strive toward their future to seek economic liberation. Otherwise, the results you hope for will only be scolding and ridicule, and you will not receive any sympathy or assistance!

Housewife Life During the Summer Vacation 247

— Zhi Yun

The family can be said to be a special period during the summer vacation. Housewives in the family should have considerable research on issues such as family hygiene, children's management, and entertainment.

During the summer vacation, the temperature is always very high, and the bacteria of various summer diseases have a good opportunity to survive and reproduce. During this period, if you are not careful with your diet and daily life, the health of the whole family can be completely destroyed. In the past, I listened to a lecture by a certain lady. She said, "Half of my time in the family is almost entirely spent on the diet in the family. I do everything myself, from washing all the vegetables to cooking them. So relatives are all secretly discussing me, saying that I have a hard life, and I hire maids, and I still have to do these things myself. I don't know that I have my quirks, and I am always extremely worried about the laziness of the maids, especially in terms of food. So in the summer vacation, even if it is to heat a dish or boil a pot of water, I must do it myself. Although I am so tireless, I have not seen any amazing results, but in ten years, the whole family has not suffered from an infectious disease once. Even in the summer vacation when epidemics are prevalent, my family is not affected at all. This cannot but be said to be the reward for my attention to dietary hygiene." Although what she said seems very ordinary, I think this is really a good rule for women during the summer vacation, so I specially introduce it. In addition, such as the proper regulation of diet, the night should not be too greedy for coolness, the family appliances should be washed and disinfected diligently, and harmful insects such as mosquitoes and flies should be killed and eliminated. All these tasks should naturally be borne by the housewives.

Children should be managed in a regular and rational manner during this summer vacation, otherwise they will wander and become wild children. I remember that a certain lady also introduced this issue. She said, "During the children's summer vacation, I think it is the best training period for the children's intellectual, moral and physical education. Therefore, during the summer vacation, I always urge them to get out of bed at about 5 o'clock every morning. At about 7 o'clock, I drive them to play in the lawn next to the house or in the park, and let them exercise as much as possible. From 9 o'clock, I order them to read, write, read newspapers and write essays. At 12 o'clock, have lunch, and in the afternoon, let them take a walk or play games, and at about 2 o'clock, make them take a nap. Wake them up in time and assign them work, such as wiping windows, washing floors, or rolling grass, etc., for one hour. Then give them a bath and rest. After dinner, take them to concerts, or watch movies, or go out for a walk, or go to the park to cool off. In every seven or eight weeks of summer vacation, it is like this. So my children not only do not neglect their studies during the summer vacation, but can make progress, and their health status when school starts is always better than when they are on vacation." It is naturally best to manage women strictly like a certain lady. If you can't learn it completely, then learning a few points is always better than not managing it at all. In short, although women do not have to go to school every day during the summer vacation, it is definitely not for letting children lead a wandering life. As a mother, you should clearly recognize this.

The issue of entertainment during the summer vacation is also very important. Entertainment is different depending on the family's living environment. So here, I can't introduce it specifically. But one thing is worth mentioning, that is, "Don't forget hygiene in entertainment." If entertainment is harmful to hygiene, it must be absolutely rejected. The best entertainment methods are going to the beach in Shanghai to bathe in the sea, or going to the suburbs for a hike, or inviting a few friends to read and laugh, or discuss family issues, or open a cold drink party, etc. These are all good summer entertainment methods.

Women in India 248

— Ying Tian

If you are an intellectual, then you must say that "early marriage" is an undesirable and evil system concerning the development of the body, as well as physical and physiological damage. Indian marriage is immersed in this environment. Usually, every Indian woman has to marry before menstruation, because of religious superstition. Menstruation is considered the most unclean thing in the eyes of Indians. Once a woman has menstruation, it is the beginning of her life as a woman. As for the origin of their early marriage, there are two legends: First, it is said that there are words in the ancient Indian scriptures that praise early marriage. Therefore, everyone enthusiastically supports early marriage. Another legend says that half a century ago, the Hui people invaded India, and Hindu believers sent their virgin daughters under the protection of men, and the evil habit of early marriage was inherited as a result.

Although, a few years ago, an Indian named "Saka" proposed to amend the early marriage case, the law was established, but there is still no solution for the general public. As a wife of an Indian man, everyone has the obligation to give birth to a son. If there is no son after three years of marriage, then they are in danger of being divorced. Based on this weakness, in the suburbs of India's largest metropolis, "Calcutta," there is a "Kali Temple." It is said that there is a Bodhisattva who grants children in the temple. Many women who are eager to have children stay in the temple, hoping to obtain a son of God in their dreams. In the middle of the night, the so-called "Bodhisattva" appears and grants them the "son of God." As a result, women who have lost their chastity are everywhere in India. This is entirely the sin of the monks! What is even more ridiculous is that this "son of God" is even more loved in the eyes of his parents?

When a woman is pregnant and approaching her due date, she is driven into a small house, cut off from contact with outsiders, except for the midwife who serves her. No one sweeps or cleans the house, and over time, it becomes extremely dirty. If the woman gives birth to a boy, she can move out of this shack earlier. If she unfortunately gives birth to a girl, then she has to live in this sea of suffering for a long time before she can escape. Some women encounter difficult labor, and the incompetent midwives, who do not understand the principles, even use things like tiles or broken glass to perform surgery. Many pregnant women's lives are lost at the hands of these hateful midwives, and infant mortality is also high. Some pregnant women even live in cowsheds filled with the stench of cow dung.

"Widow immolation" was a barbaric custom in India in the past. This ritual involved the widow covering herself with oil after her husband's death and jumping into the fiery pit during his cremation. This inhuman practice has now been banned by the government. However, the lives of widows are like death. They can only wear a plain white cloth, cannot wear rings or other jewelry, and only have one meal a day. The most tiring and lowly work is entirely undertaken by them. In their sad lives, there is no possibility of seeing them smile again.

As for their daily life, they do not see other men besides their husbands. They spend their days like cattle and horses, and must cover their heads with white cloth when going out. When traveling by car, they also have to put cloth on all sides to prevent being seen by outsiders.

The life of Indian women is no different from being in hell.

A Group Working and Supporting Themselves 249

—

Special Feature by This Newspaper

Ms. Lu Shapai Talks About Japanese Women 250

— Ji Ping

A virtuous wife and good mother is their traditional concept. Women's rights are low, only wanting to marry a good husband. Women who have accepted new ideas have a tendency to self-awareness.

Among the Chinese students studying in Japan, there are two female writers who have recently made a name for themselves in the literary world. One is Wu Manzhi, and the other is Lu Shapai. Their works are often seen in several domestic magazines, and this publication has also published them many times. Readers should be able to remember them if they are not forgetful. I have never met Ms. Wu, but Ms. Lu is currently living in Shanghai. The other day, I was introduced by a friend and had a long conversation with her for an hour. I felt that her thinking was very advanced, her knowledge was very superior, and she had a special interest in women's and children's issues. We talked too much that day, so here are just three points excerpted: (1) A review of Japanese women; (2) The characteristics of Soviet women; (3) The future of Chinese women. Ms. Lu said, "How dare a person with such shallow experience as I am make irresponsible remarks on such a big issue and make a fool of myself!" I said, "You don't have to be so polite. New women should be bold in their words and deeds, that is the spirit of a heroine."

Japanese women, on the surface, almost all seem to have virtue and womanly ways. They are the epitome of a virtuous wife and good mother, and the vanguard of diligence and endurance. However, in reality, they have no status in society at all. It is simply impossible to talk about equal rights between men and women. Japan is truly a male-centered society, which is the opposite of the situation in Europe and the United States. This is a traditional idea that has not been able to be changed to this day. But looking at Japan's education system, men and women are completely different. Strictly speaking, the education of Japanese women is a slave education! In modern countries, men and women mostly receive equal education, and co-education is very common. However, Japan has never had this example. Elementary schools may be co-educational, but there are very few middle schools and above that are. Although a few universities allow a small number of female students to enroll, they can only audit and cannot be considered official students. All female schools above the secondary level focus entirely on domestic studies, such as sewing, cooking, nursing, hygiene, etc. In addition, they teach how to treat husbands and raise children. Even the education department of women's universities focuses on home economics and children's education. There are also bride schools, that is, bride schools, which train women in etiquette for dealing with people and methods for serving parents-in-law. Although the education of Japanese women is universal, how can slave-style education improve the status of women? Japanese women have very developed professions, but there is simply not one who holds a real position of power. Most women want to marry a rich and powerful man and live a comfortable life. They are satisfied with this, so it is no wonder that Westerners say that the most backward women in the world are Japanese. This cannot be said to be an exaggeration. In the minds of men, they think that the characteristics of Japanese women lie in their gentle, docile, polite, and capable of managing the home. But on the other hand, Japanese women are narrow-minded, lack manliness, only follow their husbands, and lack an independent and equal spirit, which may be their common weakness.

I have to say, Japanese women can manage their households, raise their children themselves after giving birth, not rely on others, pay attention to children's education, and cultivate new life for the country's future. This is indeed much stronger than women in our country. There are also a few Japanese women who have accepted new ideas from Europe and the United States, and are also opposing various measures in reality, but the government monitors them very strictly and does not allow you to spread new seeds. There are also women who have gone bankrupt in rural areas and have squeezed into cities to demand a living, and have a very conscious spirit. Japan has repeatedly increased its troops to the Northeast and North China, forcing strong men to go to the front line. Women who have suffered pain see their wives and children separated, and they are in a situation where they do not know whether they are alive or dead. They are also very uncomfortable in their hearts, and often take actions to resist. Under this high pressure, there is no way to do it.

Ms. Lu deeply admires Soviet women and is constantly studying all their issues. She said that the Soviet Union is truly an emerging country, and all theories have become reality. The only country in the world where men and women are truly equal is the Soviet Union. They participate together and are active everywhere in all kinds of careers, even in heavy industry, the army, navy, and air force. In some places, the power of women exceeds that of men. This great, hardworking, and independent spirit is truly worthy of admiration. I hope that Chinese women will also imitate them. Everyone has patriotic thoughts and a passion to save the country. What are we afraid of?

She expressed the following opinions on the future of Chinese women: "China is a semi-colonial country. Before it can rise to an independent and equal position, it is difficult to solve any problems. As for the current situation, I think that Chinese women should stand under the banner of unity and work together for the national revival movement to seek a way out for the whole country. This is by no means something that a few people can do alone. We women should have rich knowledge and a superior position, but only solve the lives of one person, and have little relationship with the masses. If you look down, you will know that there are as many people waiting to be liberated as there are sands in the Ganges River. In terms of women themselves, they must be self-aware, work hard, and recognize that I am a member of society, and must not regard marriage as my profession. Men and women are equal, and each has a common responsibility. Why should I rely on men? The general women in today's society, elementary school students want to marry middle school students, middle school students want to marry college students; college students want to marry students studying abroad; this is tantamount to lowering their status and showing a psychology of dependence, which I cannot agree with. Any woman must first overcome all kinds of weaknesses before she can be accomplished." She also talked about the situation of female students studying in the East, which can be divided into two categories: (1) Hard-working and self-improving students, who have a definite purpose and come to study, and their spirit is admirable. (2) Those who are muddling through with their studies abroad, regardless of the cost of being abroad, and only seeking their own false fame. There are also many female students from the three northeastern provinces, some of whom have forgotten their motherland and recognize the enemy as their father, which is so heartbreaking!

Ms. Lu is originally from Nanhai, grew up in Guangzhou, studied in Shanghai for many years, and was a classmate of Xie Bingying, Chen Boer, and Wang Ying at the Shanghai Art University. She has been studying in Japan for two years and is studying sociology at Hosei University in Tokyo. She also likes drama, swimming, volleyball, etc. In the past six months, she has starred in plays such as "A Woman and a Dog," "Ranch Brothers," and "Infant Slaughter" at the Tsukiji Little Theater, which were famous at the time. She came back to China this time to see the dynamic of the society in the two years since she left the country. She will return to Japan soon. After graduating in two years, she is willing to devote herself to women's movement. With such a young and strong new woman, her future will definitely be very great.

Rural Women in Nantong 251

— Zheng Kangbo

I once wrote an article in the Shenbao Monthly about the lives of women in Nantong. In that article, "I divided the women in Nantong into three classes; the so-called three classes are: 1. Urban pleasure-seeking women, 2. Female students, 3. Rural women. However, in this article, there is an overly detailed description of the living conditions of the first two types of women, while the report on the daily lives of rural women is sketchy; after writing this article, I had the opportunity to edit a women's publication for a period of time. Because of this work, I have a better understanding of the lives of women in Nantong, especially in the rural areas. Therefore, I am making a supplementary account here.

If we calculate by proportion, the number of rural women in Nantong accounts for two-thirds of the total number of women in Nantong: It is extremely disappointing to talk about the education these rural women have received. Among them, those who have received compulsory education are considered to have received the highest education. Usually, most of them are illiterate. Women who have sat on the bench in private schools for a year or two can boast in the countryside. At present, except for the villages near the city, the custom of cutting hair and unbinding feet has not yet penetrated into the remote areas. In addition to sewing and cooking, these women are also a good group of helpers during the busy farming season. In the past, when Nantong cloth was still selling well, the men and women in the countryside used weaving as a sideline, and worked day and night. Therefore, a hard-working woman could get a reward of more than half a dollar every day as a result of her hard work. However, since the decline of Nantong cloth, this rich income has been lost for no reason. In today's Nantong rural areas, even self-cultivating farmers with a few acres of thin land can hardly survive. A group of small tenant farmers who are exploited by high interest rates have driven their wives and daughters to the city without hesitation. Usually, they serve as servants in the homes of the general middle class (called old maids in Nanjing). The remuneration received by this type of women is from one to two yuan per month, and those with good "extra income" can get three or four yuan, but usually it is less than three yuan.

The system of child brides is still very popular in the countryside of Nantong today. Generally, people without considerable property seek a child bride after giving birth to their children, and some even arrange marriages while still in the womb. Child brides usually get married before the age of twenty after they grow up. Some live in peace after marriage, while others undergo changes, so news of leaving their homes and villages often fills the streets.

There are also many special industries for women in Nantong's rural areas. The common one is selling fruits or food. When they encounter festivals, they collect all the seasonal or scenic items for sale in order to earn small profits. Some women with stronger physiques often come to the city to push or carry goods. They can carry or push heavy carts weighing about a hundred pounds, and they can walk like flying.

All year round, they are tempered by a life of hardship. The first month of the new year is a relatively pleasant and relaxing season for them, and this season is also abundant in terms of material enjoyment. Otherwise, the welcoming gods and temple fairs between autumn and winter every year? They can also have a good time, but that is just a day or two of revelry.

The Grief of Ancient Chinese Women Poetesses (1) 252

— Kang Tun

Parting, death, yearning for spring, growing old,

Losing love, being abandoned, mismatched, war and chaos.

Since ancient times, beautiful women have often had ill-fated lives, and talented people have often had ill-fated lives as well. But looking at the literary works of women poetesses of past dynasties, how much grief they contain, one can imagine their unfortunate encounters and inner pain. The analysis of women's grief is nothing more than parting, death, yearning for spring, growing old, losing love, being abandoned, resentment of being mismatched, resentment of war, chaos, and national subjugation, etc. This is the same for human emotions, and it has always been the same throughout the ages.

The Grief of Parting

"Sorrow is greater than separation, joy is greater than meeting," Qu Yuan has already made it clear in one sentence. In poetry, parting verses almost account for the highest number, which is truly innumerable. The most euphemistic and moving depiction of the grief of ordinary parting should be the poem on the plate by the wife of Su Boyu of the Han Dynasty:

"The mountain tree is tall, the crow crows sadly; the spring water is deep, the carp is fat; the empty granary sparrow often suffers from hunger; the official's wife rarely meets her husband. Going out to look, seeing white clothes, thinking it was him, but it was not. Returning home, my heart is sad... I often sigh, who can I tell? You have a journey, I miss you. Going out has a date, returning has no date. Tying my girdle, I miss you for a long time. You forget me, I don't know it; I forget you, the crime should be punished... Living in Chang'an, my body is in Shu, why not regret the horse's hooves and return frequently!..."

The poem on the plate is just a representative work of reluctance to part. As for the true parting verses, which are full of sorrow and penetrate the heart, the most important ones should be the song of sorrow by Wang Zhaojun when she went to the frontier, the Eighteen Songs of the Hu Jia by Cai Wenji, and the poem on the wall by Zhou Zhongmei of the Song Dynasty.

Everyone knows the story of Wang Zhaojun. As a delicate and beautiful woman, she was initially not favored in the Han Palace, but was later selected to be the wife of the Xiongnu Kingdom, far away in a foreign land, with no relatives to look up to. How sad should her heart be! Although the lament poem is only a hundred words long, her whole life experience is on paper.

"Autumn trees are luxuriant, their leaves are withered and yellow, there are crows in the mountains, gathering on the mulberry bushes, raising feathers, their appearance is bright. Having ascended into the clouds, swimming in the crooked room, leaving the palace is desolate, my body is broken, my will is suppressed, unable to fly up. Although I am fed, my heart is hesitant. Why am I alone, my coming and going is unusual, fluttering swallows, gathering far in the Western Qiang. High mountains are towering, the river water is vast, father and mother, the road is long. Alas, my heart is sad!"

Cai Wenji, as the daughter of a famous writer of a generation, encountered many national disasters. She was initially captured by the Hu people, separated from her father and far away, and became the queen of the Left Sage King. She lived in the Hu for twelve years and gave birth to two sons. Later, she was allowed to return to the Han land, but she could not take her two sons with her. She remarried and became the wife of Dong Si of Chenliu. Let us see her sorrow when she left the Han and entered the Hu:

"Leaving the Han country and entering the Hu city, losing my family and body is not as good as not being born! Wearing felt robes, my flesh and blood are shocked; taking mutton as food, I wrongly suppress my feelings. Drums are noisy, from night to dawn. The Hu wind is vast, darkening the fortress... (Third Beat)

"... Natural disasters and national chaos leave people without a master, only my fate is thin and I am dead as a prisoner. Different customs and hearts make it difficult to live; different desires, who can I talk to!" (Fourth Beat)

"If heaven has eyes, why does it not see me drifting alone! If the gods are spiritual, why do they place me alone in the north and south of the world! I have not failed heaven, why does heaven make me a different match! I have not failed the gods, why do the gods kill me beyond the desolate state!..." (Eighth Beat)

Living in a foreign land, the only comfort she had was her two biological sons. When she left the Hu and returned to the Han, the separation of mother and son was more painful than ever.

"... My body returns to the country, but my children do not follow, my heart is hanging and always hungry... The mountains are high and the land is vast, seeing you has no date!..." (Fourteenth Beat)

"... The separation of mother and son is difficult to bear, separated by the same sky is like Shang and Shen. Not knowing whether they are alive or dead, where can I find them!..." (Fifteenth Beat)

"... When I left, I missed the homeland but had no clue; when I came, I said goodbye to my children, my thoughts were vast!..." (Seventeenth Beat)

In her "Ode to Grief and Indignation," she described her initial encounters in detail, revealing her heart and lungs, making people feel infinite sorrow when reading it. This should be the swan song of the unfortunate parting of women in ancient and modern times.

Zhou Zhongmei first followed her father to Chengdu as an official, and married a husband surnamed Li. She followed her husband to Nanjing as an official. Later, her husband had a favored concubine, the family was not harmonious, and he abandoned his official position and went to Mount Hua without returning. Zhongmei took her son and lived in her maternal grandfather's house in Hefei, and could not return. When her uncle was appointed to Changsha, they were all loaded south, so she wrote her thoughts on the wall:

The Abandoned Concubine 253

— Yin

Probably because the weather is too hot, Grandpa Song's temper seems to be much worse than usual. The small fake mahogany tea table was slapped up and down, left and right by him, and it was creaking and groaning, almost losing its life under his palm.

Grandpa Song has a total of five brothers. He is the oldest, so everyone in the family calls him Grandpa Song. Grandpa Song's father, Great-Grandpa Song, had served as a few terms of telecommunications supervision and had some savings. In addition to the first wife, he also married two concubines. Grandpa Song and Second Grandpa Tao were raised by the first wife, and they came from the most upright background, so their power was also the greatest; Third Grandpa and Fourth Grandpa were raised by the first concubine. Although the first concubine had died long ago, these two grandpas were doing very well outside, so they still had a considerable status in the family; Fifth Grandpa was the youngest, raised by the second concubine. Great-Grandpa Song died as soon as he landed, so in the eyes of Grandpa Song and Second Grandpa Tao, Fifth Grandpa was really like a kitten or puppy, unworthy of attention. But in the heart of the second concubine, she had endured nine years of lowering her head and serving the small since she married Great-Grandpa Song at the age of seventeen, and she finally gave birth to this son. How could she not hope that he would be a reliance in the future? Therefore, during the initial mourning period of Great-Grandpa Song, the second concubine had a quarrel with Grandpa Song over the name on the thank you note and the thickness of the hemp clothes.

As soon as Great-Grandpa Song died, Grandpa Song was the head of the family. How could the second concubine argue with him like this without making him angry? Moreover, not only that, in Grandpa Song's calculations, when the inheritance was divided in the future, Fifth Grandpa would definitely not have a share. Unable to withstand the second concubine's quarrel, his name was on the thank you note, and there would definitely be problems in the future. Therefore, Grandpa Song was not only angry, but simply "anger arose from his heart, and evil grew from his courage." He could not wait to execute the second concubine and Fifth Grandpa immediately, but in a clear and bright world, with everyone watching, how could he commit such a poisonous hand! There was no way but to temporarily endure and slowly seek a good plan.

After a while, Grandpa Song's good plan finally came up.

One day, Grandpa Song and Second Grandpa Tao actually caught a wild man in the second concubine's room. Although this person was not naked and barefoot, and the second concubine herself cried and shouted for injustice, Grandpa Song insisted that this person was indeed her adulterer, and immediately slammed the table and stomped his feet in the hall, insisting on expelling the second concubine. The people in the family persuaded and laughed, but they all leaned towards Grandpa Song. The second concubine had no family members to help, and did not know how to use the law to clear her injustice. She could not withstand Grandpa Song's persistent coercion, so she had to let them dispose of her. She hastily packed a large bundle, left her beloved son who was still breastfeeding, and cried out with tears and snot.

The next night, Grandpa Song passed by Wenkang Bridge and saw many people surrounding a female corpse that had just been fished out of the river, making a fuss and talking about it. Without turning his head to look, Grandpa Song had already understood in his heart.

A small fishing boat came to the little river, like an ordinary艒艒 boat, which is a home that floats on the water all year round. They are an old couple. Except for sleeping, their daily life was completely moved to the ground.

They catch fish twice a day, when the tide comes and goes. They have a large net, and they娘it on the bottom of the river, facing the direction of the tide. The couple runs to the very center of the river. When the tide is high, only two heads can be seen floating in the water. They both hold a triangular pole in their hands, slowly moving their bodies in the center of the river, while moving the two triangular

Page 20

bamboo poles, going in the direction of the fish net. Because the whole body is immersed in the water, the body weight is out of balance, and the stones and glass shards in the center of the river often prick their feet, it takes at least half an hour to catch a net of fish. When they climb out of the center of the river like water ghosts, they have no time to worry about their bodies. They have to quickly收 the fish net, otherwise, their half-hour effort will be completely wasted. It is easy to put down the net, but when收 it, the net already has a large harvest. Sometimes, broken things沉 in the bottom of the river are often caught in the net together with the fish, and they are standing on the bow of the boat, using force to bend their bodies to收 the net, against the推進power of the tide. The small boat often straightens its stern as if it cannot bear the burden. Watching them收 the net, I always think of the tragic situation of seeing a fishing boat being swallowed by huge waves on the beach that year.

A big net of fish is piled on the bow of the boat. Those leaping, shining fish scales release clouds of hope in the eyes of the couple. Now they should have forgotten their wet clothes. They happily open the mouth of the net and separate the big fish from the small fish in buckets. The procedure is so fast that the sand and gravel are thrown into the river at hand, and the卜通卜通 sounds are connected. So, with smiles on their faces, they changed their clothes and went to the market to sell them.

But收 up a large net of broken things is also not in the minority. They naturally feel very disappointed after spending half an hour of effort. However, they are not afraid of hardship, and they immediately go to the bottom of the river to set up the net again, because they cannot let go of the power of the short-term tide.

Dinner is their happiest time: the old man (we can only call him that, although he himself said he was thirty-eight years old) 打 a bottle of wine, buys a little pig's head meat, or burns the small fish they caught themselves, and the couple eats dinner. Sometimes we can also hear the old man drinking their hometown's private情山歌.

Watching them net fish seems to have become a habit. I almost take my younger brother to the small river浜 every day. But in less than half a month, the fishing boat was escorted out of the country by the police. It is said that someone reported to the police station that they were翻動the river, hindering the three-year开河工程 of the opening river bureau, and affecting the drinking water hygiene of the citizens.

I thought that if these two charges were established, the old couple should be locked up in jail. Escorting them out of the country is really too cheap a punishment! But they can't fish on land. They are永家 for home, no,以水为生, then, where are they going to fish? This question troubled me for a long time, and those two simple faces often appeared in front of my eyes.

Opening for Business 265

— Ai Cha

A bustling road, a row of old buildings near a crossroads, one of which has hung up the sign "Sunshine Electroplate Studio." The June sun shines like a fireball, reflecting a dazzling light from the newly whitewashed facade.

Inside this electroplate studio, the three junior partners, all friends, are slowly preparing to start work. However, the June sun is so hot that it makes one dizzy, especially in the workshop set up on the terrace. The sun blazes down on the zinc-iron roof, filling the space with a pungent, sour smell of chemicals mixed with the heart-piercing odor of strong acids. This mixture of smells, combined with the scorching sun, makes one feel suffocated upon inhaling.

It's not yet time to start work, but the three partners already have differing opinions. Old Chen, who owns the majority of the capital, a sharp-headed, sharp-tongued fellow, looks at the other two with his head tilted. All three pairs of eyes are fixedly staring at the sun.

"The electroplate studio next door only does five-point paper (Note 1). We, on the other hand, do six-point paper."

Chen, who manages the finances, shakes his head in this way.

"What can we do? There are over thirty electroplate studios in the provincial capital. But doing five-point paper per inch is really losing money. Chemicals have gone up in price, the exchange rate for Western paper is very high, and zinc plates have risen from five and a half to eight dollars. Calculating the bare minimum, each inch of newspaper costs more than three points of paper. Wasting a little will cost four points of paper, and then there's food, rent, and other expenses. Really, it would be great if we could just earn enough for food!"

This is what Little Liu, the experienced one, says.

Old Qian blinks, and says with great confidence:

"I think that you have no work to do in the shop, just looking at the numbers, while the two of us make electroplates. You also get a share of the salary. So, the best way is for you to voluntarily do calligraphy and painting. For every order of fifty inches of electroplates or more, we give away ordinary calligraphy and painting—actually, you could earn forty or fifty dollars just by doing advertisement paintings!"

"I'm willing, but: if I write volunteer paintings, my business will also decrease."

Old Chen says a little displeased, taking a puff of smoke.

"Then! Our conditions also have to change a little!" Old Qian says, his heart filled with desires to plan for himself: "I am the dedicated expert of the photography department! Besides photography, I don't have to care about the work of electroplating, and my salary should be more than anyone else, because, my share of capital is also a lot!"

"How can that be!" Little Liu shouts angrily, his cheekbones appearing even higher: "It's okay for you to do photography, but it's not right for you not to make electroplates. Do you know that the work of electroplating is five times more than photography! You want to enjoy yourself? And you say your salary should be more than others. We don't even know how much business we have! Business is not easy to do, what salary are you talking about?"

Little Liu's eyes are also flashing with flames. He continues:

"I earn more salary than you from 'running horses' (Note 2)! I do thirty yuan of work, you only do twenty yuan of work! Really..."

In this way, he regrets pulling Old Qian into partnering in this electroplate studio at that time. Wave after wave of thoughts surge: "I really don't want to continue, I won't even take business anymore. With such disputes, I would rather let it go bankrupt."

The three people's thoughts are jumping in the waves. The sun is staring wide-eyed at the earth. They jointly feel the authority of the sun's light, and quietly sigh.

The Sunshine Electroplate Studio, under each person's private opinions, finally starts work. Everyone has their own worries. Old Chen desperately writes his own advertisement paintings, attempting to earn more income. Old Qian, this specialist technician, is a bit anxious, because the old projector is not easy to use. He spent a lot of energy, but only projected photos that were not of top quality. Little Liu is completely sloppy about his work. Business comes in slowly, and starting electroplates is slow. Supporting it like this, there is no improvement, and it shows signs of indifference. (To be continued)

Ballads 267

Qian Jingzhang Qian Zuixian Mao Jiashu

Central-West (1040) 10:00 AM to 10:45 AM

Opening piece "National Hero" (written by Gao Yang Shanren)

The situation has been changing, the importance of which we discuss. The spirit of the nation is declining, while foreign clans are becoming stronger. China originated in Kunlun. The eastward migration started from the Xia and Shang dynasties of Yu the Great. The Zhou dynasty lasted for eight hundred years, and the royal family was granted land in all four directions. The Central Plains and the Huaxia people gradually declined, and the Yi, Man, Rong, and Di tribes became wilderness. There were many miracles in the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods. The Qin Dynasty unified the entire country. Tyrannical and despotic, the Qin Dynasty was truly autocratic. The uprising of beheading the snake produced Liu Bang. He pleaded for the people and destroyed Qin and Chu. (Relying only on) Han Xin, Xiao He, and Zhang Liang. After five generations, Emperor Zhao ascended the throne. (At that time) the Eastern Kou (倭寇) were very strong and overbearing. They committed adultery, plundered, and seized everything. The coastal residents lacked peace and well-being. Fertile land became barren. A vast expanse of thousands of miles was a wasteland. National heroes rose up in time. They became generals and prime ministers like Huo Guang. (They slaughtered) ships, destroyed masts, and the invaders' heads fell. Their souls scattered, and they fled to the ocean. From then on, the coastal people enjoyed peace and prosperity. The three words "Great General" have spread far and wide. His name will be famous for ten thousand generations.

"The Good Earth" in Production 271

— Lai

Regarding the production of the Chinese film "The Good Earth" by MGM, this publication has previously recorded some information. Now, we have obtained some more news about the film, which we have translated and recorded below.

The set for "The Good Earth" is located a few miles outside of Los Angeles, with a Chinese-style village and several thatched huts, just like what can be seen in the Chinese mainland. There is also a mill turned by water buffalo and a waterwheel used to irrigate the land. It is said that the fields, spanning over five hundred acres, are entirely cultivated by an elderly overseas Chinese farmer using the traditional methods of his homeland.

The protagonist, Wang Lung, is played by Paul Muni. He wears grass sandals, a baggy blue bamboo cloth long shirt, a long red silk belt around his waist, and a small braid hanging behind his neck.

O-Lan is played by Ms. Lu Rainer. Her attire is strangely shaped, not very much like the O-Lan described in Ms. Pearl Buck's book.

There are many supporting actors from our country playing farmers and their wives. During filming, several farmers even drove water buffalo brought from their hometowns. Among them is a sixty-seven-year-old man, Li Changfu, and the chairman of the Cantonese Welfare Association in San Francisco, a person of status who likes acting.

Another noteworthy actress is Ms. Liu Lude, who is of Chinese descent. Her father is Chinese and currently works for the National Government, but her mother is American. With an Eastern-style face and speaking English, she is a purely American girl of only ten years old, playing the role of Lotus, wearing a short jacket, baggy pants, and a head full of flowers, looking just like a Suzhou prostitute.

"The Good Earth" is worth noting because, although it claims to be based on Ms. Pearl Buck's original book, based on past facts and the various observations currently underway, it will undoubtedly succeed in making a film that insults China. At the very least, it will not be very flattering to China.
